Interview with Huang Jianzhong, Director of the Hubei Education Department 128

Mr. Huang arrived in Nanjing from Hubei at noon on the 15th to attend the conference. Before the opening ceremony, he briefly discussed the outline of the Hubei Provincial Education Department's policy guidelines, which are summarized as follows:

(1) Intensify the implementation of party ideology education, military training, and Boy Scout education, and use the late Premier Sun Yat-Sen's military spirit education as the standard for school moral education to cultivate children and young people's national morality of loyalty, benevolence, love, faith, righteousness, and peace.

(2) Gradually develop rural education during the Qingxiang period, focusing on labor habits and life skills, and prepare to implement compulsory education and adult literacy education.

(3) Improve the level of secondary schools, focusing on scientific experiments and practical training, so that students in general courses can continue their studies, and students in vocational courses can serve society.

(4) Liquidate education funding in various counties and improve the salaries of primary school teachers in various counties.

(5) Reduce educational administrative expenses and expand educational program expenses.

(6) Use talent as the standard for employing people, breaking the traditional concept of so-called factions.

Interview with Huang Dujie, Director of the Xiangtan County Education Bureau 129

(1) Source of Funds

(2) Promote Schools

(3) Unify Textbooks

(4) Make Finances Public

Director of the Xiangtan County Education Bureau, Jin Dujie, spoke with reporters yesterday. The details are recorded below.

(1) Question: What is the amount and source of education funding?

Answer: The county's education funding for the 18th year of the Republic is 160,000 yuan. The sources are approximately as follows: A. Land rent is approximately 13,000 piculs of grain per year (each picul of grain is worth approximately 5 yuan). B. Land tax special donation is approximately 36,000 yuan per year. C. Deed tax surcharge is approximately 20,000 yuan per year. D. Tobacco and alcohol surtax is approximately 3,000 yuan per year. E. Pig tax and house tax are approximately 4,000 yuan per year. District education funding for the 18th year of the Republic is 220,000 yuan. In addition to donations from ancestral halls and temples, it is subsidized by county funds. Large districts receive more than 2,000 yuan, and small districts receive more than 1,000 yuan. The rest is various miscellaneous donations.

(2) Question: What about secondary education?

Answer: The county has two junior high schools, one for boys and one for girls. The boys' school has three grades, and the girls' school has two grades (there is no third grade yet). Previously, they were co-educational, but now they have been changed to separate schools for boys and girls. Even the provincial middle school has been changed to separate schools for boys and girls. The annual funding for each grade of junior high school is 1,600 yuan. Vocational schools are biased towards women. There are more than 40 such schools in the county (two private schools, and the rest are district-run). Each school is at a level between primary and secondary schools and specializes in receiving graduates of senior primary schools and those with equivalent academic ability. In addition to general subjects, there are sewing, embroidery, dyeing, and weaving. The students are very developed and cannot be accommodated. Graduates are mostly able to make a living on their own, and they are highly trusted by society.

(3) Question: What about primary education?

Answer: There are five county-run senior primary schools, distributed in cities and four townships, and three junior primary schools, one in the city and two in the townships. There is one kindergarten. There are two district-run senior primary schools and one thousand and thirty junior primary schools. There are more than ten private complete primary schools, two of which are well-managed by private individuals, so they receive provincial funding, in addition to one junior primary school established by the Junzu or Guild Hall.

(4) Question: What about social education?

Answer: The county has one library (with a reading room, a newspaper reading room, and a lecture hall), one public sports field, and reading rooms in each district, with the county responsible for a portion of the funding. There is also a circulating library system, with the districts responsible for the books and the county subsidizing a portion. Last year, there were one hundred people's schools, and this year the number has increased to two hundred. The county has a People's Education Committee to plan and promote people's education.

(5) Question: What is the salary of primary and secondary school teachers?

Answer: Secondary school teachers are paid by the hour, one yuan per hour. County-run senior primary school teachers receive a uniform monthly salary of 30 yuan, and junior primary school teachers receive 20 yuan. The salaries of district-run senior and junior primary schools are inconsistent, ranging from more than 20 yuan to as little as 10 yuan. Private schools and county schools are similar.

(6) Question: How are primary school teachers selected?

Answer: Primary school teachers have been tested twice, and only 5 or 6 percent are unqualified. Graduates of middle schools account for approximately 20 percent, graduates of A-level normal schools and the Second Normal School account for approximately 40 to 50 percent, and those who have passed the testing account for approximately 30 percent.

(7) Question: What are the characteristics of Xiangtan education?

Answer: (1) Finances are practical and public. The county school accountant is appointed by the bureau, and the faculty and staff are responsible for supervision and review. After the review, it is reported to the Education Bureau and then submitted to the county political meeting for review. The bureau's finances are submitted to the county political meeting and reported to the Education Commissioner for review. (2) The Education Bureau has set up a service station for educational supplies and books, and has signed contracts with the Commercial Press, China Book Company, and World Book Company to sell various books without aiming for profit, but charging a handling fee. Under these circumstances, the textbooks used by all schools in the county are unified. (3) The county has a population of 1.1 million, with 100,000 school-age children, of which approximately 40,000 are enrolled. Currently, eight methods for improving private schools have been established to improve private schools to assist public schools. The main points of these eight methods, which have been approved by the Education Department, are as follows: A. Examination. B. Issuance of certificates after admission. C. Numbering by the Education Committee and distribution of school locations. D. Prohibition of those who do not take the examination. E. Prescribed curriculum. F. Issuance of a report card for visiting nearby schools, limited to two visits per month. G. Subject to the guidance of district and county supervisors. Those who receive three excellent evaluations will be used as substitute primary schools. H. Teachers must attend the Summer and Winter Vacation Teacher Research Institute.

Summary of Proposals (II) 130

▲ Plan to Improve Elementary Education

(I)

1. All regulations should be set at the lowest limit and be most economical in expenditure.

2. Except for what must be uniform, attention should be paid to flexibility.

(II) Establishment

1. The establishment of primary schools and kindergartens should be based on municipal and county levels, with the central government and provinces sharing the subsidies.

2. The division of school districts should be consistent with local autonomous regions.

3. Neighborhoods, towns, villages, private individuals, and private legal entities can all establish primary schools and kindergartens, with subsidies from municipal and county governments.

4. In cities, the principle is to establish one primary school and kindergarten in each neighborhood. In towns and villages, the maximum distance for commuting to school is five li.

5. The Ministry of Education formulates the standards for establishing primary schools and kindergartens. Provinces, municipalities, special municipalities, bureaus, and departments set the minimum standards for establishing primary schools and kindergartens.

6. Schools should be established by Chinese people, with Chinese people as teachers and staff.

(III) Funding

1. Designated local funds should be consolidated and guaranteed, and insufficient funds should be expanded. The Ministry of Education will stipulate the measures.

2. The ratio of construction and equipment costs in the start-up expenses of primary schools and kindergartens should be 6:4 or 7:3. Regular expenses should be fixed per class of students or a certain annual fee per student. Salaries should account for up to 75%, and reserve funds should account for 2% to 5%. Expenses for purchasing books should be more than consumable expenses. Standards should be set by provinces and municipalities and submitted to the Ministry of Education for approval.

3. The accounting methods and property management methods of primary schools and kindergartens should be stipulated by the Ministry of Education as guidelines, and the implementation methods should be stipulated by provincial, municipal, and bureau departments.

4. Economic guarantee methods, public disclosure methods, and property handover methods should be stipulated by provincial, municipal, and bureau departments.

(IV) Construction and Equipment

1. The Ministry of Education formulates various model scopes and styles of school building construction (including lighting, ventilation, area, school site selection, and school building layout). Provinces and municipalities select several types to serve as local school building standards.

2. The Ministry of Education formulates various school building evaluation scales for use by provinces, municipalities, and counties as standards for improving school buildings.

3. The Ministry of Education formulates various model drawings of desks and chairs. Provinces and municipalities select several types to serve as local desk and chair standards.

4. The Ministry of Education formulates equipment evaluation scales for use by municipalities and counties as standards for improving equipment.

1. The rural teacher curriculum standards will be handed over to the primary and secondary school curriculum standards drafting committee, which will formulate compulsory subjects based on the needs of primary schools and can later refer to the first type of senior high school normal course to increase or decrease them for further study (see the original plan).

1. The kindergarten normal course and rural kindergarten normal course curriculum standards will be formulated by the middle school curriculum standards drafting committee.

1. Detailed curricula for various levels and types of teacher training will be formulated by national universities, national compulsory education colleges, and provincial education departments based on trial standards.

1. The curricula for various special teacher training programs will be formulated by committees organized by the Ministry of Education, and detailed curricula will be formulated by national universities or provincial education departments based on the standards.

(V) Internship Measures

1. Internships are divided into three steps: observation, apprenticeship, and trial teaching.

1. Normal schools should have special personnel responsible for planning, writing, and guidance.

1. Normal school students who fail the internship are not allowed to graduate.

1. There should be a central school as a training center.

(VI) Service and Treatment

1. The service period of graduates should be equal to the length of their training, but the compulsory period should not exceed five years.

1. If unable to serve due to illness, it can be postponed with a doctor's certificate.

1. Those who do not serve will have their tuition fees recovered.

1. Tuition and accommodation fees are waived.

1. Students who drop out halfway will have their tuition fees recovered from their economic guarantor.

(VII) Vocational Subject Teacher Training Measures

1. Normal universities and university education colleges may enroll graduates of agricultural, industrial, and commercial departments of universities, provide them with one year of training, and after graduation, they will serve as teachers in senior high school vocational subjects and vocational schools. If students in agricultural, industrial, commercial, and other colleges of various universities aspire to vocational education, they should take at least sixteen credits of education subjects from the third year onward. The subjects are stipulated by the university's education college or education department.

1. Normal specialized courses may recruit (1) graduates of specialized schools and (2) graduates of senior high school vocational courses with more than three years of suitable experience, for one year of training to serve as teachers of vocational subjects at the junior high school level.

1. Normal schools or senior high school normal courses may recruit graduates of vocational schools or senior high school agricultural, industrial, and commercial courses with considerable experience, for one year of training to serve in primary schools.

Reflections on the Second National Education Conference · Sun · Gui · Ding 131

This time, the Ministry of Education, in accordance with the resolution of the Second Plenary Session of the Central Committee last year, convened a national education conference in the capital. Although the current situation is not very peaceful, representatives from various provinces and regions have reported on time, indicating that there is indeed national unity in education, which is a gratifying phenomenon. I once attended the first national education conference convened by the University Council seventeen years ago, and this time I am also a member, so I feel that this conference is different from the previous conference in many ways. In summary, it seems that this national education conference has three special advantages:

(1) Before the first national education conference, a lot of proposals were collected from all parties. No matter what the problem was, as long as someone made a proposal, once it was reviewed and passed, it would be used as the basis for the conference's discussion.

▲ Conference Staff

(From right to left) Zheng Tianting, Director of the Editorial Section; Zhao Naichuan, Director of the Document Section; Yang Fang, Director of the Reception Section; Jiang Shaomo, Director of the General Affairs Section and Accounting Section; Peng Baichuan, Director of the Daily Editorial Section.

(Photographed by Nanjing Guanghua)

This method certainly has the advantage of gathering wisdom, but it is also inevitable that there are many complex opinions and a lack of systematic discussion. This conference is not like that. The scope of discussion is limited to the plan prepared by the Education Program Compilation Committee. This plan was compiled by the Ministry of Education, gathering many specialized scholars, and after very precise research. It is not only based on the current real situation and focuses on application, but also forms a complete system. During the meeting, he gradually used it as the basis for common discussion, step by step, in an orderly manner, which can achieve twice the result with half the effort.

(2) According to the regulations of this conference, each province may designate one director of the municipal and county education bureau or one chief of the municipal and county education section to attend the meeting. At the first national education conference, each province only had the director of the education department and one education expert outside the department eligible to attend. Comparing the two, I feel that this method is indeed better, because in addition to the director of the education department in each province, adding one director or chief of the municipal and county education bureau can clarify the actual situation of local education in various provinces and regions. During the meeting, we can also think about the implementation aspects everywhere, so as not to be isolated and commit the disadvantages of emptiness or pedantry.

(3) Although the first national education conference passed several proposals on overseas Chinese education, it did not pay much attention to it. As for Mongolian and Tibetan education, it was regarded as beyond the pale, and no one cared about it. This conference is very different. Regarding overseas Chinese and Mongolian and Tibetan education, six experts were specially hired to attend the meeting. In the plan prepared by the Education Program Compilation Committee, a plan for improving and developing overseas Chinese education and a plan for implementing Mongolian and Tibetan education were specially added as the basis for discussion during the meeting. In addition, two groups for overseas Chinese education and Mongolian and Tibetan education were added to the review committee. The above measures are sufficient to show that the second national education conference attaches importance to overseas Chinese and Mongolian and Tibetan education.

Based on the above advantages, we speculate that the results obtained at this conference will be more excellent than the achievements of the previous conference. We hope that after this conference, national education can be effectively improved, and the psychological construction we long for can be completed as soon as possible.

The Process and Key Points of Compiling the Plan for Improving and Developing Overseas Chinese Education 132

Wu Yan Yin

The Ministry of Education's Education Program Compilation Committee originally had an "Overseas Chinese Education Group." When it was in progress, the Training Department of the Central Party Headquarters convened a conference on overseas Chinese education and resolved everything. The director of the group stated that since there were resolutions from the conference on overseas Chinese education, there was no need to compile a plan on overseas Chinese education. Later, the members of the group, except for a few who gave opinions, did not turn in the plan.

After the Central Overseas Chinese Education Conference, the entire resolution of the conference was sent to the Ministry of Education. The committee felt that the entire case not only had a different format from the program's format, but also the content was not very complete. Therefore, the standing committee members re-elected personnel to draft it. After the draft was completed, it was revised several times before it became the current plan.

This plan incorporates all the resolutions of the Central Overseas Chinese Education Conference. At that time, a question arose, that is, "Since the resolution of the Overseas Chinese Education Conference has been decided by the Central Executive Committee and handed over for implementation, the government should follow it. Why should it be included in the plan and submitted to the National Education Conference?" The answer to this question is that this program is complete. All the resolutions of the Central Committee that have not been implemented have been included one by one. Of course, the resolution of the Overseas Chinese Education Conference is no exception. Moreover, in this plan, all the conclusions agreed upon by the Overseas Chinese Education Conference have been added with symbols before and after to indicate that they are not easy to change.

As for the key points of this plan, the editorial section of the National Education Conference Preparatory Committee has also put them forward separately, so I don't need to say more. But there are a few points to explain:

(1) There are differences in wording between this plan and the resolution of the Overseas Chinese Education Conference, and there are also omissions or supplements in terms of content. The modification of the wording is unavoidable and also has a basis. The original case was written in classical Chinese, and the program is all written in vernacular Chinese. This is the reason why the writing style has to be changed. Furthermore, the Overseas Chinese Education Conference repeatedly stated during the meeting that if there were any improper wording, it should be reorganized after the meeting, but what was submitted to the Ministry of Education was still the wording of the original case, and it was not seriously modified. Then, adding modifications is not aimless. Fortunately, the changes in wording are originally irrelevant to the main purpose, as long as the content does not change, even if it is changed to be more inappropriate, it does not matter. As for the content, for example, the original case regarding the consular management of overseas Chinese education matters suddenly listed the specific measures that the consulate should convene overseas Chinese groups and the education community to hold commemorative weeks alongside the abstract tasks of investigation, guidance, supervision, and promotion. It is really felt to be illogical. Therefore, the section on commemorative weeks was omitted from the plan, except for the Ministry of Education's instructions to various consuls to comply with it. Also, for example, the original case, the Overseas Chinese Education Association, was originally one of the people's organizations, but its powers included both the design and guidance of overseas Chinese education. In addition to the Overseas Chinese Education Design Committee and the education specialists of the consulates guiding overseas Chinese education, there is another design and guidance agency. The organization is redundant, and the powers are easy to confuse and conflict. Therefore, it was also omitted from the plan. There are many places in the plan where the original case has been omitted, but it does not hinder the original case itself, because the spirit and value of the original case are not in these. Also, for example, the original case did not stipulate how the 500,000 yuan and 10 million yuan of fund interest allocated by the central government each year should be used and who should distribute them. This plan supplements this, stipulating that it should be designed and distributed by the Overseas Chinese Education Design Committee. These seem to be important and should be supplemented.

(2) Some people think that this plan is generally good, but they say that there is too much said about school education. It should be simplified and only some important principles should be said. In fact, this section is compiled according to the format of the plan for improving elementary education. It is necessary to make practical regulations on the establishment, organization, construction equipment, discipline, curriculum and teaching materials, faculty and staff, students, and guidance system of overseas Chinese schools, because the so-called overseas Chinese education, in addition to administrative design, school education is really a very important center of gravity, and overseas Chinese schools are much inferior to domestic schools, and they urgently need to be improved. If this plan does not stipulate this part in detail, then it will lose its center of gravity. Some people say that the principles have been stipulated in the plan, and the methods can be designed by education administrators and school authorities in each province. I don't know that the principles are very general. Very general principles often make it impossible for people to implement them. For example, saying that teachers should be registered without saying how to register, and that teachers should be guaranteed without saying the main points of the guarantee, isn't this making it impossible for people to implement them? To implement the plan, it must be said more thoroughly. Although the content does not have to be too detailed, the procedures, the methods of handling, and the main points that should be paid attention to cannot be stipulated.

(3) Many people who study overseas Chinese education are generally satisfied with the organization section of the original plan, but they think that the center of gravity lies in the Ministry of Education establishing an overseas Chinese education department or an overseas Chinese education administrative committee, but the actual center of gravity does not lie in the overseas Chinese education department or the overseas Chinese education administrative committee, but in the consular specialists who guide overseas Chinese education (or the roving guidance specialists selected by the Ministry of Education) and the Overseas Chinese Education Association, because the Ministry of Education, the highest administrative education department of overseas Chinese education, is also responsible for the main method, and it does not matter much whether a special department or committee is established. If a special department or committee is established, but overseas consulates do not have education specialists (or do not send roving guidance specialists), and there are no education associations in various places, this is equivalent to a crab without feet. The whip is too long to reach, and what can be done? Otherwise, overseas has specialists to directly guide and education associations to help with the handling. The Ministry of Education only needs to complete it. It does not matter much if a special department or committee is not established. Overseas education specialists and local education associations are the center of gravity for directly supervising overseas Chinese education. Whether overseas Chinese education can be improved and developed depends entirely on this. This is what we should recognize.

In addition, we should know that education is not a simple problem. It is related to all politics. If other political constructions have no way, education can never have a way alone. This principle is particularly obvious and certain for overseas Chinese education. Overseas Chinese education should be supported by the country's political power. If the government cannot support it, the life of overseas Chinese education cannot be extended beyond ten or twenty years, not to mention improvement and development. The so-called support of the country's political power is not something that the Ministry of Education can do unilaterally. In addition to the Ministry of Education, at least two aspects of great help are needed:

Page 12

(1) In terms of diplomacy, overseas Chinese schools, except those in the United States, are oppressed and cannot be free in the British, Dutch, Japanese, and French colonies. The Dutch, British, and French colonies impose harsh restrictions on overseas Chinese schools, such as registration, etc. This is known to everyone. Recently, the Dutch government does not allow Chinese consuls to manage overseas Chinese education. When Chinese consuls hold graduation ceremonies in overseas Chinese schools, their attendance and certificates are also warned by the Dutch government. As for not allowing schools to hold commemorative weeks and teach the Three Principles of the People, it is even more common. The Japanese government in Taiwan does not even allow the establishment of overseas Chinese schools. If you want to set up a formal school (other than private schools), you must have a Japanese as the principal and teach Japanese. How can overseas Chinese schools be maintained under these circumstances? How can they be improved and developed? Even if there are programs and plans, and they are detailed and thorough, what is the use? Therefore, if all programs and plans are to be implemented, they must first be successful in diplomacy. It is hoped that the diplomatic authorities will not think that overseas Chinese education is not their job, and they will be afraid to retreat and perfunctorily deal with this negotiation. They should automatically investigate the attitudes and methods of each colony towards overseas Chinese education, negotiate separately at any time, and pay attention to adding a section to protect overseas Chinese education when revising treaties, in order to do their best to protect overseas Chinese education.

(2) In terms of economy, overseas Chinese are failing in business because the government has no time to protect them, and the overseas Chinese themselves do not have large-scale organizations such as management capabilities. Recently, the overseas Chinese community in Manila, Philippines, has therefore affected education funds. Many people who originally paid additional education donations are now unwilling to pay. Therefore, each overseas Chinese school is in great panic. Chen Jiageng is also almost unable to maintain Xiamen University and Jimei School, which he runs, due to the sluggish rubber business. By analogy, it can be seen that if overseas Chinese businesses fail, overseas Chinese education will be difficult to maintain. It is still difficult to maintain, let alone improve and develop. To maintain and improve and develop overseas Chinese education, we cannot only find ways in education itself, because even if the government allocates 500,000 yuan a year and raises a fund of 10 million yuan and spends its interest, it is like a cup of water to quench a cart of firewood, and it cannot reverse the fate of overseas Chinese education. It is hoped that in addition to allocating funds to subsidize overseas Chinese schools, the government will also work hard to protect overseas Chinese merchants and maintain their businesses. The Japanese government often provides special subsidies to overseas merchants and people's businesses to help them compete with foreign righteousness. They also subsidize four to five million Japanese gold each year for the rubber industry. Therefore, their rubber industry can take away Chen Jiageng's market in China, resulting in the decline of Chen Jiageng's company. In view of this, the Chinese government should find ways to assist overseas Chinese merchants, either by giving them subsidies, or by sending industrial and commercial experts to various overseas ports to guide their business, or by reducing or exempting them from fees, property, and head taxes, or by diplomatic authorities finding ways to negotiate with foreign countries to lift all kinds of restraints on their business. Otherwise, overseas Chinese merchants will not be able to stand on their feet overseas for ten or twenty years in the future. The impact will not only be on education.

Educational Opinions (2) by Gao Junshan 134

(C) Proposal for Selecting Talented Children Nationwide to Receive Obligatory Education at All Levels (1) Reasons

(1) Talented children are the elite of a nation. All future construction and development projects will come from their hands. Before having the financial resources to implement universal compulsory education, if we can select talented children nationwide within a possible scope to provide obligatory education at all levels, the effort required for primary, secondary, and higher education would be minimal, but the results would be remarkable, achieving twice the result with half the effort. Moreover, the contribution of this group of outstanding individuals to society in the future, if it could be represented in monetary terms, would greatly exceed the cost of their education. Looking at it with a broader perspective, the education of talented children is not only a policy of immediate relief but also a system with lasting value.

(2) Democratic countries need leaders. The emergence of leaders is not based on origin but on talent and ability. If these exceptionally gifted children do not receive proper education to inspire their genius, they cannot fully express their intelligence. Some may even be tempted by bad environments and go astray. The negative aspect is the waste of talent, while the positive aspect is that their talent and ability may be used for wrongdoing. This becomes an obstacle to national security. Conversely, if we educate them in an ideal way, we can increase social effectiveness.

(3) A leader must have the personality of a leader. Without good education, they may become indulgent or selfish. Once they attain a high position, they will exploit it to satisfy their desires, like the warlords of the past. Selecting talented children for education is to cultivate our future ideal leaders with noble personalities.

(4) Talented children are not only future leaders of the masses, but some will also be future academic leaders. They are creators and inventors. Future contributions in literature and art, scientific discoveries, advancements in material civilization, and increased production will all rely on their strength.

(5) If we use a slightly higher standard when selecting (assuming one person out of every hundred, with an IQ above 130), the total number nationwide would not be very large. The state should be able to handle this economic burden.

(6) According to the results of experiments in special classes for gifted children attached to elementary and secondary schools in various places such as California and New York in the United States, the results are very significant, and the expenses do not need to be increased. Because of early graduation, expenses are sometimes reduced instead. Therefore, this kind of facility is indeed economical in education.

(2) Methods

(1) The Ministry of Education should hire educational experts to define the standards and principles for talent, compile testing tools, and formulate implementation procedures, as well as educational guidelines and procedures.

Huang Shiheng, Director of the Hunan Provincial Department of Education

(Photo taken by Nanjing Guanghua)

(2) Each province should invite several experienced educators to investigate talented children in various cities and villages based on the defined standards. Talented children within schools will naturally attract the attention of investigators, but this will only account for a small number. They should also find ways to investigate children who have not yet entered school to avoid the regret of missing gems.

(3) The selection procedure should use the most economical and precise method. Otherwise, the scale is so large that it will become impossible.

(4) The selection criteria should be high, so the number will not be too large, and the state can afford this expense.

(5) After selection, those who have not entered school should be ordered to enter school immediately. Those who are capable of entering middle school or university but cannot afford to do so should be allowed to attend school for free. Those from extremely poor families should also be given appropriate subsidies for books and stationery.

(6) Schools at all levels that talented children enter should have special facilities to give them the opportunity for free development, so they are not constrained by ordinary children.

(Note) Some people think that this kind of method is not in line with the spirit of equality. In reality, it is not. The saying "All men are created equal" is just a self-deception for religious figures because unequal phenomena in society are so obvious. Therefore, they have to use excuses to comfort themselves and reassure people. But where is there such a thing? The most unequal thing is the difference in innate abilities. Genius and idiocy are extremely obvious phenomena, but these phenomena are the most impossible to imagine. Since there is no way to imagine, we are happy to take this opportunity to use it. In an organized group, the position of each member cannot be without difference. Once there is a difference, classes are produced. What way is there to stop this? This kind of organized group needs different talents. The highest position cannot but be given to the highest talent. Since the emergence of talent follows the laws of nature, and society has to rely on talent, then our selection of talent and providing obligatory education at all levels is to use talent to increase social efficiency and not to enhance the class system.

▲ Proposals to set up special classes in primary and secondary schools

(1) Reasons

(1) The great difference between individuals has been confirmed by scientific methods. Therefore, children of the same age of nine, one is still having difficulty in the second grade, and one can already enter the sixth grade. The current school system mostly divides classes according to age and the length of enrollment, not according to ability. Moreover, the facilities in teaching are based on the ability of ordinary children. Neither the disabled nor the gifted children are taken care of. The impact of this kind of education only affects the mediocre group of people. The extremes on both sides do not receive the same benefits. This is a great waste in teaching. After the special classes are set up, this kind of waste can be eliminated.

(2) Compulsory education is a right that every child should enjoy, not just for mediocre children. Although disabled children, talented children, and mediocre children have the same obligation to pay taxes, everyone does not enjoy the same rights. This is mistreating the disabled and the gifted children.

(3) Disabled children are always lagging behind in a class, constantly running behind their classmates. No matter how hard they try, the results are inevitably failure. In addition to shame, anger, and resentment, they will inevitably become eccentric or pessimistic. Because gifted children find their schoolwork too easy, they cannot be motivated to move forward. They will inevitably develop lazy habits. Moreover, living above others and gaining without labor can also develop an arrogant heart. These are all contrary to the principle of cultivating personality. But if special classes are set up, then the disabled children will not feel ashamed of themselves compared to others and feel despair, and the gifted children can compete with those of equal ability without being depressed.

(4) Most of the subjects in school are textual, symbolic, and abstract. Disabled children lack the ability to understand abstract things, so textual education is often futile. If disabled children are put into special classes and taught separately, then teaching materials and methods suitable for their abilities can be used. (To be continued)

National Scout Inspection News 135

▲ Continued Arrival of Scouts

A total of over 300 scouts from Zhejiang, Qingdao, Shandong, and other places continued to arrive for the national scout inspection on the 15th.

▲ Chairman Chiang Approves Allocation of Barracks for Research Class

For this general inspection, it was originally planned for scouts from various places to stay at the camp in Beijing. However, due to the continuous rain in recent days, there was a lot of water in the camp, and there was no way to camp. Therefore, the reception section of the office invited them to stay in various schools and public places separately. On the 15th, the office found it inconvenient to manage and liaise with them in various places, so it contacted the National Government. Chairman Chiang approved the allocation of a part of the barracks of the military officer research class as a camp for scouts arriving in Beijing. It is said that it can accommodate three or four thousand people. The move-in began in the afternoon.

▲ Appointing Evaluation Committee Members

The organizational regulations of the National Scout Inspection Evaluation Committee have been promulgated and implemented by the Scout Headquarters. The office sent letters inviting Hu Hanmin, Dai Jitao, Sun Ke, Chen Guofu, Zheng Wu Ting, Liu Luyin, Chen Lifu, Shao Yuanchong, Jiang Menglin and other nine people to be members of the evaluation committee for the first general inspection and the grand camping event.

▲ Organizational Regulations of the Evaluation Committee

Organizational Regulations of the Evaluation Committee: (1) The Chinese Scout Headquarters, in order to hold the first National General Inspection and Grand Camping of the Chinese Scouts and to evaluate the results of various competitions, the commander shall hire three to seven members of the Central Committee to organize the Evaluation Committee for the first National General Inspection and Grand Camping of the Chinese Scouts. (2) Under the committee, there shall be fifteen judges, three reporters, and six recorders, who shall report and record the evaluation. The personnel shall be hired by the commander. (3) The duties of the committee are as follows: (A) to verify the qualifications of participants in the competition; (B) to formulate and implement various evaluation standards and rules; (C) to evaluate the results of the general inspection, grand camping, and various competitions; (D) to resolve disputes concerning the general inspection, grand camping, and various competitions; (E) to announce the results of various evaluations; (F) to issue prizes and souvenirs. (4) All supplies and forms required by the committee shall be formulated by the competition section of the temporary office. (5) The committee shall be established one day before the general inspection, and the regulations shall be announced and implemented by the Chinese Scout Headquarters.

▲ Song Ziwen Presents Silver Shields

Cai Song has prepared two silver shields to present to the Soviet scouts. The words "Loyal Heart Guards the Country" are engraved on one, and the words "National Spirit" are engraved on the national scout and a letter has been sent to the Scout Headquarters for commemoration.

▲ Four Shanghai Scout Regiments Have Not Arrived in Beijing

They have all reported to the headquarters one after another and stationed in various places. Soviet Scouts Camping 136

▲ Closed and Awarded Prizes Yesterday

▲ Depart for Beijing Today

The first Grand Camping of the Jiangsu All-Day Scouts, since the opening ceremony on the 13th, has been continuously rainy, so that various competitions cannot be held due to the slippery ground. Moreover, due to the urgent schedule for going to Beijing, all competitions have been cancelled. Although this time there was no competition, the spirit of each team was always shining before our eyes, which has aroused the attention and admiration of the community. They will definitely have good results in the National General Inspection in the future. At 2:00 p.m. yesterday, the closing ceremony was held and prizes, commemorative medals, and certificates were awarded. The details are recorded separately as follows.

▲ Closing Ceremony

(1) Play music; (2) Sing the Party song; (3) Pay the highest respect to the Party flag, the national flag, and the portrait of the Premier; (4) The chairman respectfully reads the Premier's will; (5) Silence; (6) The chief evaluator reports; (7) Inspection; (8) Admonition; (9) Awarding prizes; (10) Sing the Scout song; (11) Shout slogans; (12) Ceremony.

Circle the field three times; (13) Play music and dismiss.

▲ Participating Representatives

Chairman Ye Chu of the provincial government, Li Mingyang, member of the Hu Puan Committee, Zhang Daofan, Ye Xiufeng, Zhu Jianbai, Wu Baofeng of the provincial party headquarters, Mrs. Chen He, Ms. Zhao Lingxian, representatives of various institutions and organizations, and about 7,000 people.

▲ Chairman Ye Gifts Food

Chairman Ye of the Jiangsu Provincial Government believes that the scouts held their first grand camping during the continuous rain, and the members of each regiment never reduced their brave spirit due to the rain, which is commendable. He specially gifted 915 boxes of canned food, with each member getting one box on average, to encourage them.

▲ Chief Evaluator's Report

Chief Evaluator Zhang Daofan reported, roughly saying that today is the last day of the Grand Camping. Because of the bad weather these days, we could not compete. Today's awards are based on the standards of camping, cleanliness inside the camp, discipline in the camp, morning exercises, service spirit, and neat uniforms. This time, there are more than 100 large prizes and more than 1,000 small prizes. When distributing the prizes, we can proudly say that there is no partiality. Although there are grades in each country, everyone can get a little prize to encourage them. Our scouts take service as their duty and do not want rewards. Several regiments reported too late this time, and originally there was no reward, but this delay was mostly due to waiting for the train to buy tickets, etc., which could not be done smoothly. Waiting for the train is impossible to imagine, so everyone is rewarded. The 58th Regiment has very good results, but their qualification as instructors cannot be compared with ordinary schools and scouts, so they are evaluated separately and given separate awards without comparing them with other regiments on average. This is the evaluation committee's process of evaluation. I hope that those who get more prizes will strive for progress, and those who get fewer prizes will work harder. Tomorrow we will leave for Beijing to participate in the National General Inspection. I hope everyone will work hard to win glory for Jiangsu Scouts and set an example for national scouts.

▲ Award Situation

After the admonition of the two provincial government members Ye and Li, the awards were presented by Zhao Jinxian, wife of the Director of Education Chen Hexian. Chen Bangcai, the director of the camp, brought them close to the front of the stage in order. Each group had a total of five regiments. For a time, the music was ocean-like, and the applause was endless. The representatives of each award-winning regiment were all overjoyed, and Mrs. Zhao Lingxian, with a smile on her face when issuing the awards, completed the awards. Then, the captains of each team distributed the canned food donated by Chairman Ye and the thousand commemorative medals from the Shandong Provincial Government.

▲ Grade and Prizes

Although this grand camping was not able to compete due to the rain, the results of the daily morning exercises, camping cleanliness, discipline, cooking, and service spirit were evaluated by the evaluation committee. The 58th regiment of Suzhou Zhongshan Sports College was the best. However, because the regiment is a training class dedicated to training scout teachers, there are special circumstances, and good results have been achieved. It cannot be treated the same as other regiments. However, because the regiment has served the camp for days and is quite commendable, the Grand Silver Cup donated by Commander-in-Chief Chiang, the Silver Shield of He Yingqin, and the Grand Award Flag of Wang Zhengting of the Ministry of Education were awarded to encourage it. This time, the evaluation procedure is divided into eight grades. Except for the 60th Regiment of Jiangdu, which is ranked in the first grade, the other grades include 357 regiments. All participants have prizes, but the number is large and the size of the silver shield. In addition to the awards received by each regiment, the evaluation meeting believed that the service personnel such as the business director of the camp director, the deputy director of the information team, the captain and deputy captain of the public security team, and the director of the hospital were able to perform their duties in the continuous heavy rain, and they should also be rewarded. The remaining award flags were given to them as a souvenir. As for the thousand commemorative medals donated by the Shandong Provincial Government, each member of the team received one. Chen Guofu, a member of the Central Executive Committee, specially donated a complete collection of Premier's works this morning, which was given to Mr. Chen Bangcai, the director of the camp, after discussion by the evaluation committee. In the future, if more prizes are received, the outstanding teams in the province will be rewarded for participating in the National General Inspection. Today, the prizes for each team will be distributed in turn by Zhao Lingxian, wife of Chen Hexian, Director of the Department of Education.

Two Kinds of Awards from the Science Society This Year 137

▲ One for Archeology

The two kinds of awards of the Chinese Science Society this year, one is the Gao Woman Memorial Award, the scope of the thesis is physics, and the eligibility is limited to students of domestic universities and vocational schools. Record of the Three Organizations Convening Talks with Principals of Private Secondary Schools and Above 138

The Municipal Propaganda Department, the People's Training Committee, and the Municipal Education Bureau jointly convened a meeting with principals of private secondary schools and above in this city at 2 PM the day before yesterday. Attendees included Chen Dezheng, Head of the Propaganda Department of the Shanghai Special Municipal Committee of the Kuomintang and Director of the Municipal Education Bureau, Tong Xingbai of the People's Training Committee, and Chu Fucheng, President of the Faculty of Law University, totaling more than ten people. Chen Dezheng presided over the meeting, with Gu Zenghong serving as the recorder.

The meeting began as scheduled. Chairman Chen Dezheng reported, stating in brief: "Today, the Municipal Party Department Propaganda Department, the People's Training Committee, and the Education Bureau have jointly convened this meeting with principals of secondary schools and above. I will first explain the reasons for this gathering and then invite all of you to express your opinions. Before explaining the reasons, the three organizations must first apologize for the abruptness of this meeting and express our gratitude for your punctuality.

"Recently, numerous reactionary elements, such as Communists, Nationalists, Reorganizationists, and disillusioned politicians, have taken advantage of the rebellions of Yan and Feng to engage in extensive activities, attempting to create social unrest to achieve their selfish goals. They are constantly seeking opportunities for reaction. The recent disturbance on Beijing Road is a clear example. You are all likely familiar with the details of this event, so I need not elaborate. In short, these are reactionary elements seeking to sacrifice the lives of others to ignite chaos. The unfortunate deceased were sacrificed, a truly tragic event. We are paying close attention to these types of incidents.

"We must recognize that under the current circumstances of internal and external troubles, China must achieve peaceful unification to save our nation from peril. The first step is for everyone to focus on their respective duties and fulfill their responsibilities. As this group of reactionary elements attacks the central government, we must do our utmost to assist the central government in preventing all reaction. Yesterday's disturbance on Beijing Road was merely the first act orchestrated by reactionary elements. Unfortunate events may, indeed, unfortunately recur. To prevent problems before they arise, the three organizations have convened this meeting.

"Reactionary elements are very effective in their propaganda. They cleverly create pretexts, such as the Free Alliance, the Humanitarian and Relief Society, and the April 8th Massacre Relief Association. Upon examination, their actions are directly or indirectly directed and incited by the Communist Party. They use appealing names to incite the public. For example, the Free Alliance targets schools. They invite seemingly famous, disillusioned scholars to give lectures at various schools, inciting young students with unsettled blood. The Party then stirs up unrest to achieve their goal of creating a society of terror.

"You are all educators and, of course, everyone seeks freedom. However, we must clearly understand the true meaning of freedom. What kind of freedom does the Free Alliance advocate? They use the beautiful name of individual freedom to incite the minds of young students, aiming to undermine the freedom of the nation and the people. I ask you, before the freedom of the nation and the people is secured, shouldn't individuals sacrifice a portion of their individual freedom to strive for the freedom of our nation and the people? Once the freedom of the nation and the people is destroyed, where will individual freedom come from? The Free Alliance has the Communist Party as its background. They do not want the freedom of the nation and the people. We must clearly recognize their true colors and not be deceived by their appealing names. Young students with unsettled blood are easily incited, so I ask you to pay special attention to preventing their activities to safeguard the peace of society and the nation.

"Furthermore, they say that the Ministry of Education and the Municipal Education Bureau are depriving young people of their freedom to study. Their reason is that the Ministry of Education has recently closed private universities. The Ministry's crackdown on private schools is entirely for the sake of young people's pursuit of happiness, preventing them from being deceived by universities established for the purpose of extorting money. I ask you, should schools have complete curricula and orderly facilities? Is it permissible to disregard everything and pursue other goals under the guise of running a school? The Ministry of Education wants young students to acquire genuine knowledge, so it is strictly cracking down on private universities, truly seeking to protect young students' education. However, the reactionaries are using this as an opportunity to create disturbances and spread many alarming rumors to incite the public. I hope you will inform your faculty and students not to fall for these unfounded rumors.

"The Humanitarian and Relief Society also has a good name, but their humanitarianism is to incite ignorant young people to create tragedies, and their relief is to take other people's money to fund their reactionary activities. This kind of propaganda is not likely to be effective in the knowledgeable education sector, so they focus on the worker aspect. However, we must also pay attention to preventing them. I hope you will be mindful of students' actions. Yesterday, the protesters on Beijing Road claimed to be supporting the labor unrest at Jardine Matheson in Nanjing Xiaguan. In fact, the Jardine Matheson labor unrest has been completely resolved. The central government has already published the details in the newspapers. However, reactionary elements are still using this as an excuse to create trouble, resulting in the tragic deaths of innocent young people. The reactionaries want to use the Jardine Matheson labor unrest to create a second May 30th Massacre, using other people's lives as opportunities for their activities. Their intentions are truly hateful.

"I heard that students from various schools participated yesterday. I ask you to strictly prohibit students from participating in these kinds of events in the future. In twenty-one days, May will arrive. There are many commemorative days in May, making it a month of many disasters. Reactionary elements will certainly take advantage of this May, with its appealing names and potential for rallying support, to engage in extensive activities. I now ask you to pay attention and cooperate with us to prevent the major conspiracies of the reactionaries. When a small number of students from your schools participate at that time, I hope you will make efforts to persuade them. The Party and the government will have ways to address all national humiliations and public welfare issues. Your schools generally have large student populations, and it is difficult to ensure that every student is reliable. You should be responsible for preventing students from acting outside the bounds. If you encounter difficulties, you can report to us at any time. You, as principals, can of course be responsible for the overall actions and expressions of the entire student body. Although reactionary elements are conspiring to create chaos, if we make efforts to prevent them, their activities will certainly be greatly hampered. The sole purpose of the three organizations convening this meeting today is to address this issue. Please pay attention."

Tong Xingbai of the People's Training Committee gave a speech, stating in brief: "The reasons for the three organizations convening this meeting have been explained in detail by the chairman, so I need not repeat them. The chairman has already explained the passive prevention methods. I will now say a few words about the proactive prevention methods. First, we must change our mindset. Most people in education believe that the responsibility for implementing Party ideology lies with the Party Department. This view is wrong. We must understand that education is a tool for implementing the Three People's Principles. Those running schools should share the responsibility of implementing the Three People's Principles with the Party Department. Second, we must prevent crises lurking within. Elementary school students, after being guided by teachers, can indeed feel the influence. However, the situation is different in middle schools and universities. This is because the various social science textbooks on the Three People's Principles are incomplete. Most schools use textbooks on Communism, Nationalism, and other ideologies. These anti-Three People's Principles textbooks have a significant influence. Although schools have Party ideology courses, the hours are few, and they cannot compete with the effectiveness of the anti-Three People's Principles textbooks. We acknowledge that textbooks should be carefully considered. Although textbooks on various subjects have various ideologies, we should summarize them with the Three People's Principles. Currently, we are far from this ideal. This is a crisis in Party ideology education. Teachers should use the Three People's Principles as the guiding principle to critique various theories. Then, students will naturally not be influenced by various theories and embark on the path of reaction."

Li Yuanshan (Tongde Obstetrics School) stated in brief: "I deeply admire the three organizations' concern for social stability and school unrest. Our school has very little connection with research on the relationship between medicine and social problems. Students also have very little contact with society. If there are any reactionary events in the future, we will make efforts to prohibit them."

Xia Jinlin (Melon Middle School) stated in brief: "Please provide guidance from the three organizations on the dates of school closures, class suspensions, and student participation in commemorative events."

Wang Daoyuan (Shanghai Art College) stated in brief: "Our school has district branches that can prevent all reactionary propaganda."

Qian Yimin (Huiling Middle School) stated in brief: "Our school's location is remote, and we have very little contact with society."

Gu Zhizhong (Minzhi Middle School) stated in brief: "The work of reactionary elements is very secretive. It is really difficult for school authorities to prevent these actions. My personal opinion is that Party members should bear more responsibility and secretly resist reactionary propaganda. It is easy for classmates to know about the actions of reactionary elements. We can ask the Party Department to instruct Party members in the student body to pay close attention to reactionary elements among their classmates."

Fan Peiyu (Suzhou Shanghai Middle School) stated in brief: "Our school has received reactionary publications. We should ask the Party Department to pay attention to the mailing of these reactionary publications."

Zhang Juansheng (Nanyang Commercial High School) stated in brief: "To prevent reaction, we should do more propaganda work. I believe the Party Department can send more people to various schools to conduct propaganda during commemorative weeks, making it easier for students to be influenced."

Su Yingjie (Minli Middle School) stated in brief: "There are many commemorative days in May. Disputes often arise between school authorities and students. The Education Bureau should be notified this year to avoid disputes. At the same time, the student union should also be notified."

Zhao Shifu (Zhonghua Vocational School) stated in brief: "The propaganda of reactionary elements is really very powerful. There are too few Party ideology courses, and there are not enough Party ideology teachers. I hope that Party ideology teachers can not only understand Party ideology but also understand various ideologies and be able to accurately critique various theories so that students are not incited by other ideologies. It seems that Sunday can be used to study Party ideology."

Zhu Fucheng (Faculty of Law University) stated in brief: "The schools mentioned in the chairman's report should naturally pay attention to ensuring that the eventful May passes peacefully. Inevitably, there will be a small number of reactionary elements in each school. According to the ministry's order, there will be no holidays in May. I believe that during the commemorative days in May, each school can suspend classes for one or two hours to hold commemorations so that students do not participate in off-campus commemorations. At the same time, the Party Department can send people to give speeches, which may allow May to pass peacefully."

The chairman stated in brief: "The Ministry of Education issued a circular on July 1st last year, stating that there will be no holidays for any commemorative days in May. For the May 1st Labor Day meeting, various agencies will send personnel to participate but will not have a holiday. For the May 3rd Party Department-organized commemoration, various agencies will send personnel to participate but will not have a holiday. For the May 4th student-organized commemoration, the Party Department will send personnel to provide guidance but will not have a holiday. For the May 5th Party Department-organized commemoration, various agencies will send personnel to participate but will not have a holiday. For the May 9th Party Department-organized delegate assembly, there will be no holiday. For the May 6th Party Department-organized commemoration, various agencies will send personnel to participate but will not have a holiday. For the May 30th Party Department-organized delegate assembly, there will be no holiday. Each school can follow the ministry's orders and will not be notified again."

Mr. Chu's suggestions are very good. Each school can hold commemorations on campus. Party ideology education does not end with the Three People's Principles courses. We should pay attention to discipline and facilities. Educators should use schools to civilize and make it easier for students to be influenced by the Three People's Principles. This is the true spirit of Party ideology education. I hope you will pay attention. The use of holidays can be determined by each school based on their circumstances. Regarding the issue of the insufficient number of Party ideology teachers and the difficulty in shouldering the school's finances, the Party Department and the Education Bureau will devise good policies. The sole purpose of the three organizations convening this meeting today is to prevent the conspiracies of reactionary elements and to ensure that the education in this city can progress according to plan."

Municipal Education Bureau Orders Municipal Schools' College Guidance Forms Not to Be Sent to the Bureau 139

The Municipal Education Bureau issued an order to municipal schools yesterday, stating: "The College and Career Guidance Committee of this Bureau, to assist schools in implementing college and career guidance, has created three types of forms: the Student Interest Survey Form, the College-Bound Student Survey Form, and the Career-Bound Student Survey Form. These forms have been circulated to schools for purchase from the Bureau. However, a small number of schools, after students have filled out the forms, immediately compile and send them to the Bureau. This is inconsistent with the College and Career Guidance methods. According to the methods, after the forms are filled out, they do not need to be sent to the Bureau. Schools can disassemble and summarize the forms filled out by students and implement guidance based on the results of the forms and the procedures stipulated in the methods. At the end of the semester, the schools can submit a report to the Bureau on the guidance process and results."

New Book Published by the World Society 140

▲ Marriage Revolution, etc.

The World Society at No. 130 Yong'an Lane, North Sichuan Road, Shanghai, is making considerable efforts in academic work. In recent years, it has published many books. Recently, it has published three books: Marriage Revolution, Unveiling Japan's Conspiracy Against China, and The Economy of the United States After the Great War. Marriage Revolution is Russell's latest masterpiece. His views on sexual morality and his claims on marriage have a revolutionary spirit. Chapters such as female liberation, the neutral status of humans, romantic trials, marriage, sexual problems and personal happiness, divorce, population, prostitution, and eugenics all have special contributions. The translation is vivid and makes for great reading. Each volume is 95 cents and is sold by major bookstores on Shanghai's Fourth and Sichuan Roads and major bookstores in various ports. In addition, the World Monthly, Volume 3, Issue 3, published by the Society has already been released. The main items include articles on China's industry in the past seventy years, the trade war between countries in Manchuria, research on India's finances, Germany's repayment of reparations in fancy ways, the fundamental questions in the Soviet Union's Five-Year Plan, an investigation of Austria's Social Democratic Party, the centuries of bloody struggle in Nicaragua, the world economy and economic policies in the third quarter of 1929, modern family problems, education in Soviet Russia, French materialism, Byron's childhood, and world news. Each volume is 25 cents. The annual subscription is 2 yuan and 50 cents. It is sold by the Commercial Press in various provinces and major bookstores in various ports.

News from the Far Eastern Games 142

(1) Name to Be Changed

The Tokyo Dispatch on the 9th stated: "When the Eighth Games were held in Shanghai, Dr. Oseas of the Philippines informally suggested at the conference of the China-Japan-Philippines Committee that the name of the Games, originally called the Far Eastern Games, would be inappropriate when countries such as India participate in the future. It should be changed to the Oriental Athletic Championships." At that time, this suggestion was not approved. Therefore, it was decided to discuss it again at this Games.

(2) Volleyball Still Uses Old Rules

For the volleyball rules of this Games, Japan proposed using the current rules stipulated in Japan. However, China and the Philippines firmly expressed their opposition. As a result, the old Far Eastern rules must still be used. These rules are called the "First to Score Out" system. The court is seventy feet long and twenty-five feet wide. For women's competitions, there are twelve official players and two substitutes. The men's net is seven feet six inches high, and the women's net is six feet six inches high.

(3) Boxing Not Open to the Public

The boxing competition at this Games is limited to official athletes only and will not be open to the public. Foreigners residing in Japan are not allowed to participate.

(4) Japan's Baseball Team

For the baseball competition at this Games, the representative players from Japan will be determined by the Japan Sports Association. It has been decided to invite the six major universities of Waseda, Tokyo, Keio, Meiji, Rikkyo, and Hosei to compete at the Meiji Jingu Stadium. The winner will participate in the Games.

Also, the United Press Tokyo dispatch on the 15th stated: "In the second game between Keio and Meiji Universities in the Six Universities Baseball League, Meiji avenged their defeat with a score of four to two. In the second game between Waseda and Teikyo Universities, Waseda won again with a score of nine to four." Another dispatch said: "The final game between Keio and Meiji Universities, which had one win and one loss, has been temporarily postponed. The game originally scheduled for this afternoon between Hosei University and Rikkyo University has been postponed due to rain."

Municipal Stadium Continues to Organize Small Volleyball League 146

The Municipal Public Sports Stadium, in light of the successful Municipal Elementary School Volleyball Competition held last summer, is now organizing the second Municipal Small Volleyball League and plans to expand the scope, dividing the teams into two groups, A and B. The players in Group A should be 60 to 62 inches tall and weigh 95 to 110 pounds. Each team can register 14 players, with 9 players playing on the field. The court regulations are: Group A: 60 feet long, 30 feet wide; Group B: 48 feet long, 24 feet wide. The net height for both groups is 6 and a half feet. The competition time is after class, without hindering students' studies. Registration begins on April 14th and ends on May 4th. It is reported that notices have already been sent to various elementary schools to solicit participation.

Local News

Municipal Executive Committee Prepares to Celebrate the Anniversary of the National Government's Establishment of the Capital in Nanjing 147

▲ Convening a Celebration Meeting with Representatives from All Walks of Life on the 18th

▲ Holding a Public Rally for Punishment of Yan Feng

April 18th marks the third anniversary of the National Government's establishment of its capital in Nanjing. Nanjing is the capital designated by the Prime Minister. During the Xinhai Revolution, the Prime Minister was elected as the President, and the central government was located here for fifteen years. In 1926, the Party vowed to launch the Northern Expedition and recover Wuhan. The National Government moved from Guangdong to Wuhan. On April 18th, 1927, in accordance with the Prime Minister's will, Nanjing was established as the capital. The Propaganda Department of the Shanghai Special Municipal Executive Committee of the Kuomintang is actively preparing for the celebration, formulating propaganda outlines and commemorative methods, which have been disclosed and distributed to various lower-level Party departments. It is scheduled to hold the Shanghai All-Sector Celebration of the National Government's Establishment of the Capital in Nanjing and Anti-Rebel Propaganda Rally at the Penglai Grand Theater in the South City at 9 AM on the 18th of this month. The commemorative methods are recorded as follows:

▲ Commemorative Methods (1) At 9 AM that morning, the Headquarters will convene representatives from all levels of Party departments, agencies, schools, groups, etc. (4 representatives from each), to hold the Shanghai All-Sector Celebration of the National Government's Establishment of the Capital in Nanjing and Anti-Rebel Propaganda Rally at the Penglai Grand Theater. (2) In addition to representatives participating in the commemorative meeting convened by the Headquarters, the Pudong, Meilong, Zhenru, Wusong, and Jiangwan districts should separately convene local residents to hold convenient commemorative gatherings. (3) All propaganda teams from all levels of Party departments should set out to give speeches. (4) Propaganda materials should follow the propaganda points, propaganda outlines, and propaganda plan issued by the Headquarters. (5) Leaflets will be produced and printed by the Headquarters and sent directly to the Party departments in each district holding commemorative gatherings. It would be even better if the Party departments in each district could print their own leaflets, but they must be sent to the Headquarters for review in advance. (6) Slogans should be reprinted or copied by all levels of Party departments. (7) The order of the meeting is as follows: (1) Opening music. (2) Sing the Party anthem. (3) Pay the highest respects to the Party flag, national flag, and the Prime Minister's portrait. (4) The chairman reads the Prime Minister's will. (5) Silence. (6) The chairman reports. (7) Speeches. (8) Proposals. (9) Chant slogans. (10) Adjournment. (8) The following slogans are prescribed: (1) Nanjing is the capital designated by the Prime Minister. (2) Nanjing is the memorial site for the resurgence of the Chinese nation. (3) Nanjing is the political center of the country. (4) Nanjing is the memorial site for the Purification Movement. (5) To commemorate the establishment of the capital in Nanjing, we must strive for political tutelage and construction. (6) To commemorate the establishment of the capital in Nanjing, we must eliminate the remaining warlords. (7) Down with Yan Xishan, the Northern Warlord who is full of feudal ideas. (8) Down with Yan Xishan, the warlord who is undermining peaceful unification. (9) Support Commander-in-Chief Chiang and thoroughly eradicate the remnants of the warlords. (10) Support Commander-in-Chief Chiang and eliminate all reactionary forces. (11) Long live the Kuomintang. (12) Long live the National Government. (Produced and printed by the Propaganda Department of the Shanghai Special Municipal Executive Committee of the Kuomintang)

Bureau of Public Works Reduces Taxes 149

▲ Decision Effective July 1st

▲ Abolition of the Two-Percent Additional Surtax

▲ Land Tax Changed to Seven Per Thousand

The municipal surtax in the Public Concession, commonly known as the Police Surtax, was originally 14%. From July 1st, 1927, it was increased to 16%. The municipal surtax in areas outside the Concession, that is, the Extra-Settlement Roads Area, was also increased from 12% to 14%. At that time, the Chinese taxpayers believed that the surtax had not been agreed upon and rose up in opposition. As a result, more than 40 stores were forced to close. Later, Yu Qiaqing served as a mediator, and the two-percent surtax was paid under protest under the name of "Two-Percent Additional Surtax". According to news from the Bureau of Public Works, the Board of Directors of the Bureau of Public Works has decided to abolish the two-percent additional surtax and reduce the land tax from eight per thousand to seven per thousand, effective July 1st of this year. The budget for this year has also been revised accordingly.
