Central Government Orders Shanghai Joint Business Association to Cease Activities 153

▲Legal Provisions Do Not Include Organizing by Road

The Training Department of the Central Executive Committee issued an order yesterday to the Shanghai Joint Business Association, stating: "The Ministry has received a petition forwarded by the Central Secretariat from the Shanghai Special Municipality All Roads Business Community General Federation, requesting the Shanghai Special Municipality Party Headquarters to rescind the order to cease the Federation's activities, etc. Upon review, the Chamber of Commerce Law and the Industrial Guild Law, as well as their implementing regulations, have all been promulgated. Business organizations in all localities should be managed according to the law and should not object. However, the Chamber of Commerce Law and the Industrial Guild Law do not include provisions for establishing an association based on roads as units. The organization of the Shanghai Special Municipality All Roads Business Community General Federation is, therefore, difficult to sustain legally. In addition to instructing the Shanghai Special Municipality All Roads Business Community General Federation to accept the order of the Shanghai Special Municipality Party Headquarters to cease activities and to reorganize in accordance with the law, the Ministry hereby orders the Association to immediately and strictly instruct the Shanghai Special Municipality All Roads Business Community General Federation to comply and not delay under any pretext." A letter to this effect has been prepared and forwarded, hoping for compliance.

Factory Law Not to be Delayed 154

▲Executive Yuan Rejects the China Industrial Association's Request

The China Industrial Association, citing many difficulties in implementing the Factory Law immediately, specifically petitioned the Executive Yuan for a delay in implementation. The Executive Yuan, finding the reasons presented insufficient, issued an order to the Association, refuting each point. The original order stated: "Regarding the request of the Association for a delay in the implementation of the Factory Law, the Executive Yuan has instructed the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to review and handle the matter, and has notified you accordingly. Furthermore, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce has replied stating: 'The Secretariat of the Executive Yuan has forwarded a telegram from the Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui Silk Cocoon General Association, requesting that the Factory Law be temporarily suspended for one year, which has been instructed to be reviewed and handled by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce. Now, a written request for a delay in implementation has been submitted, which should also be forwarded to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for review.' Upon detailed review, the reasons presented by the Association for requesting a delay in the implementation of the Factory Law are not very sufficient. The points are clarified below: (1) Article 8 of the Factory Law stipulates the principle of working hours. The original petition argued that there would be unfairness. Although the principle of working hours is uniformly limited to eight hours, for work that requires extended hours, the Factory Law allows for up to ten hours. If a factory has guard work that requires extended hours, it can be handled according to the regulations in that article. (2) Article 13 of the Factory Law prohibits night work for female workers. The original petition worried that this would affect the livelihoods of women and reduce the production capacity of cotton mills. The original intention of the law is that female workers' bodies, social morality, and family management are negatively affected by night work. Therefore, this regulation aims to improve the lives of most female workers. Before the implementation of the Factory Law, cotton mills could hire male workers, train them, and have them replace female workers. Thus, night work could be performed by male workers, and the two-shift system could still be applied, without reducing the production capacity of cotton mills. (3) Articles 15 to 18 of the Factory Law stipulate holidays and salary provisions. The original petition argued that there were too many holidays and increased burdens. The holiday dates have been approved by the National Government, with a total of seven national holidays per year. The method of paying daily workers for holidays and Sundays should be handled in accordance with legally valid collective agreements or work contracts. In the absence of such agreements or contracts, the method should be determined based on whether the work is long-term or short-term. This has been communicated by the Ministry to the provincial and municipal governments, instructing factories to be informed. There are already established guidelines for holidays and holiday pay for daily workers. Long-term workers should have regular and special leave, and wages should be paid during leave. This is necessary to relieve fatigue and improve work efficiency. The original petition only considered the economic aspects of factories and was biased. (4) Article 37 of the Factory Law stipulates that female workers receive pay during maternity leave. The original petition argued that there was no time limit and that there would be many abuses, and that paying wages during leave would increase the burden on factories. The article clearly stipulates that work should be suspended for eight weeks before and after childbirth, which does have a time limit. Childbirth is a natural duty of women, and the maintenance of their livelihood during childbirth is an obligation that humanity owes to women. Therefore, the factory should bear the cost of paying wages during maternity leave. (5) Chapter 10 of the Factory Law stipulates factory meetings. The original petition argued that labor and capital are on equal footing, infringing on factory management rights, and that Article 50 stipulates that disputes will be provoked. The agreed methods in this chapter cause factories to lose their legal benefits over property rights. Factory management is of common interest to both labor and capital, and it is appropriate for labor to participate in discussions. How can this be considered an infringement of management rights? Article 50 is intended to communicate the opinions of labor and capital and eliminate labor-capital conflicts. The original petition believed that none of these provisions did anything other than provoke disputes, but it is unclear on what basis this was said. The number of representatives to factory meetings is equal for labor and capital. Since the method of agreement is adopted, the resolution must be agreed upon by both parties. In this way, the legal benefits of the factory's property rights will not be lost. In summary, the Association did not understand the meaning of the law and did not provide detailed explanations, which inevitably led to misunderstandings. It is proposed that the Association be notified and instructed to prepare before the Factory Law is implemented, so that it can be followed when the time comes. Please review the various reasons for the Association's request for a delay, and whether they are justified."

Exchange of Old Public Bonds for New Public Bonds 159

▲The Bureau of Finance Proposes Exchange Measures

▲The Municipal Government Approves Announcement in the Newspaper

The Municipal Bureau of Finance, for the purpose of reorganizing old public bonds, has proposed measures for exchanging old public bonds for municipal public bonds, which have been approved by the Municipal Government for publication in the newspaper. The exchange will be entrusted to the Municipal Bank for rapid implementation. The measures are as follows: (1) Bridge and Road Public Bonds: (1) Holders of bridge and road public bonds issued by the former Zhabei Public Works and Patrol Donation Bureau may exchange them for municipal public bonds at the Shanghai Municipal Bank. (2) The exchange rate for bridge and road public bonds to municipal public bonds is 0.725 silver taels per yuan. (3) Bridge and road public bonds may be exchanged for municipal public bonds limited to the following types and amounts of principal and interest: (A) Un-drawn principal of 73,200 taels; (B) Drawn but unclaimed principal of 1,700 taels; (C) Unclaimed fourth-term interest of 45 taels; (D) Unclaimed fifth-term interest of 565 taels; (E) Unclaimed sixth-term interest of 755 taels; (F) Unpaid seventh, eighth, and ninth-term interest of 12,020 taels. (4) Holders of bond certificates falling under item A of Article 3 may combine the old bond certificate with the coupons for the seventh, eighth, and ninth terms and exchange them for municipal public bonds of equivalent value. If there is any remaining amount less than five yuan, it will be refunded in cash. If the old bond certificate has unclaimed interest for the fourth, fifth, and sixth terms, as mentioned in items C, D, and E of Article 3, they will be refunded in cash. (5) For bond certificates falling under item B of Article 3, in addition to exchanging the interest for the seventh and eighth terms, as mentioned in item F of Article 3, for municipal public bonds, the principal and the interest for the fourth, fifth, and sixth terms, as mentioned in items C, D, and E of Article 3, will be refunded in cash. (6) For the interest for the seventh and eighth terms, as mentioned in item F of Article 3, in addition to handling the attached interest coupons for undrawn and drawn but unclaimed bond certificates according to Articles 4 and 5, a separate interest payment voucher for the seventh and eighth terms will be issued for the bond certificates that have been redeemed. This voucher may be exchanged for municipal public bonds at the exchange rate. (7) Each exchange will be based on the total amount of bond certificates held by the bondholder and not on the number of bond certificates. That is, the total amount of bond certificates exchanged each time will be calculated together, and each bond certificate will not be calculated separately. (8) In addition to the principal and interest specified in Article 3, interest for the fourth term and above, and the eighth term and below, will not be calculated. (9) Old bond certificates will be exchanged for municipal public bonds at face value with no discounts. (10) If the exchange occurs after the due date for the interest of a certain term of the municipal public bonds, the coupon for that term should be detached. (2) Road Administration Public Bonds: (1) As the deadline for claiming outstanding road administration public bonds issued by the former Zhabei Public Works and Patrol Donation Bureau has passed and supplementary issues have been made, holders of these bonds must first register with the Bureau of Finance to conclude the matter. The registration period is from (date) to (date). Bonds that are not registered by the deadline will be invalid. (2) After registration is completed and the actual outstanding amount is determined, the Municipal Bank will be notified to exchange the bonds based on the registered certificates. (3) This exchange of old public bonds for municipal public bonds is limited to registered bonds. Bonds that are not registered will be invalid. (4) This exchange of old public bonds for municipal public bonds only accounts for the principal and does not account for interest. (5) This exchange of old public bonds for municipal public bonds uses the exchange rate of 0.725 silver taels per yuan. (6) Each exchange will be based on the total amount of bond certificates held by the bondholder and not on the number of bond certificates. That is, the total amount of bond certificates exchanged each time will be calculated together, and each bond certificate will not be calculated separately. (3) Yu Garden Public Bonds: The original amount of these public bonds was 10,000 yuan, of which 4,000 yuan has been repaid. The remaining outstanding principal is 6,000 yuan. The interest for the third term (due in June of this year) is 480 yuan, plus the unclaimed principal and interest for the second term, which is 264 yuan, for a total of 6,744 yuan. The exchange method is the same as Articles 7, 9, and 10 of the bridge and road bonds.

Ship Radio Operators May Issue Temporary Licenses 160

The Radio Administration Bureau of the Ministry of Communications stipulates that, except for radio operators serving in radio stations directly under the Ministry of Communications, radio operators on all other ship radio stations must pass an examination and be issued a license before they are allowed to serve. The Bureau has drafted temporary regulations for issuing licenses to ship radio operators, which have been submitted to the Ministry of Communications for review. Before the regulations are promulgated, the Bureau has obtained the Ministry's approval to temporarily issue temporary licenses to facilitate ship radio operators, in order to facilitate navigation. The Bureau's approved Ministry Order No. 1621 is recorded below: "Informed of the report. Ship communication is related to sovereignty. The temporary regulations for issuing licenses to ship radio operators have been revised and will be promulgated and implemented soon. Before these regulations are promulgated, all ship radio operators who request exemption from examination and issuance of temporary licenses due to being in transit should be temporarily accommodated and issued temporary licenses first, provided that the shipowner issues a certificate to prove their identity. Once the ship sails to Shanghai, they should take a supplementary examination. Those who fail the examination should have their licenses revoked to prevent abuse and facilitate navigation. You are hereby ordered to comply."

Resolution of the Case of French Sailor Stabbing Chinese 161

▲Fulfillment of Three Conditions

The case of the French sailor stabbing a Chinese person in the Catholic Church on the 30th of last month has been reported in previous newspapers. Subsequently, Mr. Du Yuesheng, in his capacity as a director of the French Concession, mediated with the trade union of the Commercial Press Publishing House. After several rounds of negotiations, both sides made concessions, and the three immediate measures directly related to the case were reluctantly narrowed down and resolved. The conditions agreed upon by both parties are as follows: (1) Mr. Du Yuesheng, in his capacity as a director of the French Concession, will convey the French Concession authorities' deep apologies to the trade union of the Commercial Press Publishing House. (2) The offending French sailor will be handed over to the commanding officer for punishment, with a five-year imprisonment. (3) Mr. Du will transfer 5,000 yuan for medical and recuperation expenses to the trade union of the Commercial Press Publishing House. Mr. Du then sent Mr. Wei with a letter of apology and 5,000 yuan in cash to the trade union of the Commercial Press Publishing House on Fourth Road on the evening of the 11th. After receiving it, the union distributed the money, with Song Derong receiving 3,350 yuan for medical and recuperation expenses, and Zhou Fugen receiving 1,250 yuan. On the 14th, a meeting of all group leaders was convened to report on the negotiation process. The union members were satisfied after receiving the report. The union also reported to the Municipal Party Headquarters for record. The report is recorded below: "Report on the matter of Song Derong, a member of this union, being stabbed by a French sailor. On April 1st, Comrade Wang Yongliang was dispatched to submit a report to your headquarters, requesting that you urgently telegram the government to file a serious protest. More than ten days have passed without a response. At this time of public anxiety, Mr. Du Yuesheng, in his capacity as a director of the French Concession, repeatedly sent representatives to request negotiations with this union. This union initially felt that this matter was of great importance and that we should not proceed with mediation without instructions from your headquarters. However, in fact, since the incident occurred, public opinion has been restricted and support has been very weak. Fearing that further delay would cause obstacles, we had no choice but to reluctantly narrow the scope and compromise on the three immediate measures directly related to the case after several rounds of negotiations with Mr. Du's representatives and Mr. Du himself. As for the two fundamental demands, which target imperialists around the world, we still request that your headquarters forward them to the Central Government and lead the national public with the spirit of revolution to confront all imperialists in order to achieve thoroughness. Although this union's strength is small, we dare to be in the vanguard and obey your instructions. Respectfully submitted."

▲ Exports Exceed 20 Million Yuan

According to statistics on Japan's trade with China in March released yesterday by the Japanese Embassy's Shanghai Office, exports (i.e., Japanese goods shipped to various parts of China) amounted to 40 million yuan, exceeding imports by 20 million yuan. Anti-Opium Association Protests Planting of Opium Seedlings in Southern Fujian 168

According to news from the Chinese National Anti-Opium Association, its investigation department received reports from citizens in various counties in Southern Fujian stating that opium prohibition is severely lax in the area. It is said that Southern Fujian has historically been a major opium-producing region. However, in recent years, due to strict government orders prohibiting opium, local authorities in various counties have paid some attention, and opium seedlings in various places have decreased slightly. Unexpectedly, recently in Jinjiang and Nan'an counties, more opium seedlings have been discovered. The county authorities not only fail to take action to suppress it, but instead collect fines based on the size of the opium-growing areas, ranging from several thousand to several hundred yuan. Areas planting opium are allowed to harvest the opium sap. Whether the area has already planted or is being cleared, fines must be paid, resulting in numerous abuses and widespread complaints. The local people are suffering immensely and have specifically appealed to the association for assistance. The association has sent a letter to the Central Opium Prohibition Committee requesting a thorough investigation. The letter is recorded below: To the esteemed Central Opium Prohibition Committee, Greetings. We received a report from citizens of Quanzhou, Fujian, stating that villagers in Maping Township of Jinjiang County and Xinying Township of the 38th District of Nan'an County in your province are planting opium seedlings in the hope of making large profits. The authorities in the two counties not only fail to strictly suppress and investigate, but instead collect fines and allow harvesting, which clearly violates the national government's opium prohibition laws. We request a vigorous investigation and handling of the matter. The planting of poisonous seedlings has long been strictly prohibited and investigated by the government, and the regulations for the eradication of opium seedlings in various counties have been repeatedly emphasized. However, in Jinjiang and Nan'an counties, where opium seedlings have been discovered, the local government only collects fines and does not eradicate them, which clearly constitutes condoning and accepting bribes. We are sending this letter to your esteemed committee requesting an investigation and response. The future of opium prohibition is of utmost importance. Respectfully submitted, Chinese National Anti-Opium Association.

Records of the Jisheng Society's Relief Work Conference 169

Due to the urgent and frequent reports of disasters from various locations, the Chinese Jisheng Society held a relief work conference at its headquarters yesterday. Attendees included Chairman Wang Yiting, Vice Chairmen Xu Qianlin and Huang Hanzhi, and more than thirty committee members. After the meeting began, Chairman Wang briefly outlined the main points of the meeting and asked the relief work director to report on the disaster situation in various regions, distinguishing between urgent and non-urgent cases, and discussed the following actions: (1) The disaster situation in Taiwan is extremely severe. Last year, the society provided relief to Linhai, Ninghai, and other counties, allowing disaster victims to avoid hunger and cold amidst wind and snow. If spring relief is not continued, the previous efforts will be wasted. It was therefore decided that Director Feng Shaoshan should, after finishing the work in the Oujiang region, lead thirty-six relief workers to Taiwan to handle spring relief. (2) Spring relief in Baoying is being organized, the disaster situation is severe, and the need for funds is significant. Director Liu Shulun has repeatedly sent letters requesting additional funds. It was resolved that, as the originally planned amount is insufficient for distribution, an additional 6,000 yuan will be approved. (3) The disaster situation in Shaanxi Province is extremely tragic, and the number of refugees is increasing daily. If spring relief, including the provision of seeds, is not continued, the starving people will be left to die. It was resolved that, in addition to the existing relief workers stationed in Shaanxi, Director Zhang Xianqing should be publicly appointed to lead a number of relief workers to depart immediately and travel from Pingliang to Shaanxi. (4) Disaster victims from Shaanxi and Henan are congregating, transportation is blocked, and food supplies are cut off. For the sake of fundamental relief, immigration policies must be actively pursued. It was resolved that the society will be responsible for a certain number of immigrants from the province, who will be sent from Fengtai to outside the customs. Someone suggested that the four items currently proposed should be implemented concurrently and require urgent fundraising. In addition, there are dozens of places requesting relief that cannot be reached, which is regrettable. At a time when disasters are occurring everywhere, we have reached a point where there is nothing left to provide relief. However, we, living in safety, should think of danger and use our sincerity to appeal to heaven for harmony. Only by making extra efforts, hoping that society will follow suit, gathering more enthusiastic talents, and raising more relief funds can we save more people and create more good karma. This is what I would like to contribute to my colleagues. Someone else suggested that although the construction of river dikes and dams is being carried out in various regions, it is not an immediate solution to the urgent needs. If local philanthropists can vigorously promote agricultural irrigation, it will greatly benefit the people's livelihood. Its contribution is not small. Today, only by rewarding the production of agriculture and industry can we truly save the country. We should do it whenever possible within our ability. The public expressed sympathy. Finally, the economic committee spoke, stating that there is a significant shortage of funds at the meeting and that several tens of thousands of yuan should be advanced first to facilitate progress. It was publicly agreed to discuss and implement this matter at length. The bell rang, and the meeting adjourned.

Tragic Fire in Nanshi Yesterday Morning Claims Three Lives 174

Mother and Daughter Ascend to Save Grandmother

Three Generations of a Family Suffer Calamity

▲ Careless Use of Stove in Early Morning

▲ Staircase Burned Through in an Instant

▲ Deceased Known for Their Good Character

▲ Neighbors Deeply Mourn

Yesterday morning at 6:10 AM, a fire broke out at No. 4, Ankang Lane, No. 48 Caojia Street, south of Caojia Bridge in the western city of Shanghai, destroying a three-bay, two-story Shikumen house and claiming three lives. The details are as follows:

▲ Family of Several Members. No. 4, Ankang Lane is a three-bay, two-story Shikumen house, and the house in the back row is also a three-bay, two-story Shikumen house. Both houses belong to the Gan family and are uninsured. The Gan family resides in the house in the back row, while the Shikumen house in the front row is rented to Zhang Bosun. Zhang is from Shanghai and his father, nicknamed Zhang Meimei, is from the Jing'an Temple area. He worked as a stable master at the Longfei Carriage Company in the Public Concession for many years. Zhang Bosun currently works at the Tianjin World Film Company. His family consists of his elderly mother, Zhang Liu, 61 years old, his wife, Zhang Wang, 39 years old, his daughter, Zhang Cuiying, 17 years old, his widowed sister-in-law, Zhang Huang, 31 years old, and Wang's four-year-old niece, Daxin. His son, Ziqin, is also 17 years old, the same age as Cuiying, and is currently an apprentice at a rice store in the northern city.

▲ Careless Use of Stove. Zhang Liu's bedroom was located on the upper floor behind the living room, while Zhang Huang lived in the east wing room on the upper floor in front of the living room. The second-floor room between them was sublet to a Gu family (a couple and an eight-year-old daughter). The second-floor room in the rear section of the east wing was rented to a Zhang family (a couple). The second-floor room in the west wing was occupied by Zhang Bosun's wife, Zhang Wang, and daughter Cuiying. The first-floor living room was jointly used. The first-floor room in the west wing was rented to Liu Zhang, and the first-floor room in the east wing was rented to the Zhong family. At 6:30 AM yesterday, the maid, Feng Guibao, of the Liu Zhang family got up and lit a wind stove in the rear section. After the charcoal fire was lit, she went to the tap in the courtyard to fetch water. When she returned, the room was already on fire, and the items beside the stove were quickly engulfed. She desperately cried for help and ran to the front section, dragging Liu Zhang out of bed. At that time, only the maids of each family had gotten up; the rest were still asleep. Because the fire was raging, the staircase was burned through in an instant. Because the staircase was located in the rear section of the west wing, everyone upstairs was trapped with no escape route after being awakened. The Gu couple immediately took their eight-year-old daughter, and Zhang Wang, holding her four-year-old daughter, jumped from the window and escaped unharmed, but they were injured and hired a car to go to the hospital for treatment. Zhang Huang and the four-year-old girl were unharmed, which was very fortunate.

▲ Sacrificing Themselves to Save Grandmother. Zhang Wang and Zhang Cuiying had already escaped downstairs when they suddenly heard Zhang Liu upstairs crying for help. Because Zhang Liu had suffered from paralysis last year and was unable to walk, she was confined to her bed all day. Therefore, the mother and daughter bravely risked their lives to ascend the stairs again, intending to rescue the grandmother. However, the fire had already penetrated the roof, resulting in the grandmother, daughter-in-law, and granddaughter, three generations of the family, all perishing in the disaster. Their pet dog, which was upstairs, was also burned to death. The fire was extinguished after about an hour, destroying a three-bay, two-story Shikumen house. Because it was surrounded by high walls, the neighboring houses were not affected, but the two Shikumen doors of the Gan family's house in the back row were reduced to ashes. The stone strips around the doors were scorched and cracked.

Alarm. The West District Fire Brigade was nearby. Upon hearing the alarm, Chief Xia immediately led employees to the scene with a fire engine and connected to the water supply to extinguish the fire. Soon, fire brigades from various districts also arrived and poured water on the surrounding area to extinguish the fire. After the firefighters went upstairs and rescued Zhang Liu, Zhang Wang, and Zhang Cuiying, all three were already dead. Their bodies were placed in the alley at the entrance. The three had mostly suffocated from the smoke. Their heads and limbs were intact, but Cuiying's waist and Zhang Wang and Zhang Liu's faces and hands were burned.

▲ Taken to the Station for Preliminary Examination. After the incident, the police took the Liu Zhang family's maid, Feng Guibao, the two landlords (i.e., Zhang Bosun's family)'s maid, Qu Wushi, and the Zhong family's maid, Cai Fengshi, a total of four people, to the Second Precinct, Second Branch Police Station. Director Meng questioned them. According to Liu Zhang, she is 59 years old, from Shanghai, and has only one daughter. She recruited a Liu man as her son-in-law, who is now serving in the military and is not in Shanghai. Her daughter had just arrived in Shanghai the day before yesterday and is currently staying with relatives in Wenyuan Lane in the French Concession. This morning, I had not gotten up yet. According to the maid, Feng Guibao, she lit the stove carelessly, causing the fire, etc. When questioned, Feng Guibao, 26 years old, from Songjiang, stated that she had only been working as a maid for Liu Zhang for three days. This morning, after getting up, I went to the rear section to light the stove to boil water. When I carried the kettle to the tap to fetch water, I saw the room was full of fire. I was terrified and cried for help, waking up my mistress (referring to Liu Zhang) and escaping, etc. Qu Wushi, 31 years old, from Yangzhou, stated that she had only been working as a maid for the Zhang family for over ten days. This morning, after getting up, I finished washing the chamber pot and was about to go upstairs when I suddenly saw the staircase filled with fire. I was terrified and cried for help. At the same time, I poured two buckets of water onto the fire, trying to extinguish it, but it was a drop in the bucket. I had no choice but to flee for my life, etc. Cai Fengshi, 50 years old, from Taicang, stated that her master (referring to the Zhong family) had just moved in on February 26th of this year. I have been working for the Zhong family for a long time. This morning, a fire broke out upstairs. I had already gotten up, but there was no way to extinguish it. I could only shout to the people inside to escape quickly, etc. Director Meng obtained their statements and instructed them to remain for investigation to ascertain the true cause of the fire before making a decision. Qu Wushi and Cai Fengshi, being uninvolved, were released.

▲ Examining the Bodies. Patrolman Jin Qiren from the 22nd Precinct reported the incident to the District Court for an inquest. At about 3 PM, Inspector Liu Pingfan, commissioned by the court, arrived with examiner Shen Xiqing to conduct the inquest. They confirmed that Zhang Liu, Zhang Wang, and Zhang Cuiying had died from fire and completed the autopsy report, ruling that the relatives of the deceased should collect the bodies separately for burial. A huge crowd of people came to watch. When the judge was conducting the inquest, Zhang Liu's daughter, Fan Zhang (named Xiudi), rushed to the scene upon hearing the news and cried bitterly. The bodies were placed on planks covered with cotton padding and reed mats, appearing extremely tragic. The neighbors in the area all said that the deceased were very good people and that their fate was truly unfortunate.

Gambler Embezzles Public Funds and Asks to be Sentenced to Death 175

▲ Claims He Has No Face to See Anyone

▲ Words Expressing Desire for Death are Quite Sad

▲ If Only He Had Known This Would Happen

▲ Those Addicted to Gambling Should Wake Up Early

Shen Jiatai, from Shanghai, was employed by the Haiwei Foreign Firm on Jiujiang Road in September of last year, serving as an accountant. However, he was addicted to gambling, constantly losing. His monthly salary was not enough to cover his losses, resulting in significant debts. At the end of last year, he embezzled 1,089 taels, one mace, and nine candareens of account money collected by the firm, as well as 139.4 yuan of the firm's electricity bill payable to the Radio Telegraph Bureau, to cover his debts. Fortunately, this was not discovered. However, his gambling habit did not change, and his methods of embezzlement changed with the times. He did not embezzle account money but signed a check for 1,000 taels in the name of the firm's foreign manager, David, and fraudulently obtained cash from the Hongsheng Money Exchange on Sichuan Road. He went to the gambling den, hoping to win and cover up his previous misdeeds. However, he lost everything and returned empty-handed, finally regretting his actions. He was deeply afraid that the foreign manager would discover his misdeeds, resulting in even more severe punishment. Therefore, he confessed the matter the day before yesterday, hoping to be forgiven. However, David, upon hearing his confession, considered it impossible to forgive and reported it to the police station, which sent detectives to arrest Shen. Yesterday, he was taken to the Special District Local Court, where Judge Xu interrogated him. The Hongsheng Money Exchange also knew the details and hired lawyer Jiang Baoli to attend the court to request the return of the 1,000 taels embezzled by Shen, equivalent to 1,386 yuan in foreign currency. When questioned, Shen Jiaqin fully admitted to all the accusations and stated that he had no face to see anyone and requested the court to sentence him to death. His words were quite sad. It is truly a case of "one wrong step leading to eternal regret." Judge Xu concluded the interrogation and ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody pending sentencing on a scheduled date.

Fu Pingui Abandons Wife and Marries Her Younger Sister 176

▲ Wife Sues Him in Court

▲ Demanding 300,000 Yuan in Alimony

▲ Both Parties in Reconciliation

Fu Pingui, a wealthy merchant residing at No. 759 Xiafei Road in the French Concession, previously married Shao Aiqin as his wife. However, several years ago, Fu had an affair with his wife's younger sister, Shao Jinchi, and formally married her at a certain clan hall. Afterwards, he abandoned his legal wife, Shao Aiqin, ignoring her. Therefore, Shao Aiqin hired lawyer Li Xinyang to file a lawsuit in the French court, accusing Fu Pingui of abandonment and bigamy, and requesting compensation for alimony. After the presiding judge approved the summons, the defendants, Fu Pingui and Shao Jinchi, did not appear. According to the plaintiff's lawyer, the first defendant married the plaintiff in the first year of the Republic of China. After they were married, they were initially harmonious. Later, the first defendant became involved with the plaintiff's younger sister, disregarding the crime of bigamy, and secretly married her. The defendants not only abandoned the plaintiff but also abused the plaintiff together with Shao Jinchi. As a result, the plaintiff was forced to borrow money to make a living. The plaintiff is seeking 300,000 yuan in alimony. Since the defendant has 240,000 yuan in deposits at the Bank of Communications and the defendant's residence is worth over 200,000 yuan, the plaintiff is seeking to provisionally seize the defendant's deposits to protect the plaintiff's interests before the case is concluded. The defendants' lawyers, Lu Shaozong and Lu Jianai, argued that the defendants were unable to appear in court due to illness and requested a postponement of the trial. The plaintiff's lawyer strongly opposed the provisional seizure and requested its dismissal. It was ruled that the decision on the provisional seizure would be made later. Another summons was issued yesterday. Judge Zhu ruled that as the case concerned the issue of alimony, all deposits at the Bank of Communications could not be moved before the case was concluded. Following this ruling, the lawyers for both parties stated that both parties were in the process of reconciliation and requested a postponement of the trial. The judge approved the request and postponed the hearing for two weeks.

Special District Court Hears Kidnapping Case Yesterday 177

▲ Wushi Elementary School Student Kidnapped

▲ Testified in Court Yesterday About the Kidnapping

▲ One of the Kidnappers Still Trying to Deny Involvement

▲ The Small Leather Shoes Were Also Presented as Evidence

Chief Inspector Feng Baishun of the General Police Headquarters previously arrested four kidnappers: Chen Kangsheng, Zhu Guoliang, Qian Yiqing, and Shi Maozi, and recovered the hostage, Guan Xiong, a nine-year-old boy from Yongjia District, who resided at No. 358 Pike Road. The boy was handed over to his family, and the four kidnappers were detained pending interrogation, as previously reported.

▲ Boy Tells How He Was Kidnapped. Yesterday afternoon, the case was heard in the third court of the Special District Local Court. The presiding judge was Sun Yuan. First, the police detectives brought the defendants to court.

The child was questioned about the kidnapping. According to the child, he was a second-grade student at Wushi Elementary School. On the afternoon of the 24th of last month, at 4 PM, he was on his way home from school on Xinzha Road when he met the defendant Chen Kangsheng and was tricked into staying at his house for two days. He was then taken to a hotel near the North Railway Station for one night and later moved to the Daxin Hotel. During the day, he and Chen would go out to play. He knew Chen before. He had never seen the other defendants before.

▲ Testimony of the Daxin Hotel Tea Waiter. The tea waiter of the Daxin Hotel, Mao Hesheng, testified that the defendant Chen Kangsheng brought the boy and checked into room 45 at about 8 PM. They then went out together and returned to the room at midnight. The next morning at 9 AM, they went out again. At 8 PM that night, they returned again. That night, Chen went out again to buy American ginseng, leaving Sun alone in the room. The boy then cried loudly and called out for his brother. I went into the room to comfort him. Not long after, detectives arrived and took the child away.

▲ Qian Yiqing Was the Mastermind. The defendant Chen Kangsheng confessed that the case was masterminded by Qian Yiqing. Qian gave me 50 yuan beforehand. Zhu Guoliang was also invited by Qian. He also hired a lawyer to defend himself.

▲ Zhu Guoliang Invites Friends to Testify. Zhu Guoliang stated that he worked at the Commercial Press. At 10 PM on the 28th of last month, he was arrested near the Qianjiang Guild Hall on Wenjian Si Road on his way home from work. He refused to confess to the kidnapping and hired lawyer Ye Fucong to defend him. Qian Yiqing stated that he arrived in Shanghai from Yixing by train on the night of the 28th to visit a friend named Zhong at the Daxin Hotel and was arrested. He denied any involvement in the kidnapping. Wang Jianqiu, a staff member of the typesetting department of the Commercial Press, testified on Zhu Guoliang's behalf, saying that Zhu was very honest and would not commit kidnapping.

▲ Detective Describes the Arrest. Ma Xiaozhi, the detective in charge of the case, reported the circumstances of the arrest of Chen and Zhu, stating that he first arrested Chen Kangsheng at the intersection of Wenjian Si Road and North Henan Road on the night of the 28th. Zhu was about ten yards away from Chen when he saw Chen being arrested and looked alarmed, so Zhu was also arrested. At the time, Chen admitted that Zhu was an accomplice. A pair of small leather shoes found in Qian Yiqing's suitcase were presented as evidence, and it was said that Qian had bought these shoes for the child to wear. At this point, the court ordered the defendants to be remanded in custody and adjourned the hearing to a later date.

The Municipal Government Consults the Ministry of Railways to Relocate the Songhu Branch Station 179

▲ To Maintain Traffic Flow on Baoshan Road

Baoshan Road in Zhabei is a vital transportation artery in northern Shanghai. However, the Songhu branch line of the Jinghu-Hangzhou Railway bisects it, causing inconvenience to vehicles, pedestrians, and other travelers. Recently, the number of steam passenger trains traveling on the Songhu line has increased to seventy-four trips per day, more than double the previous number. Consequently, traffic congestion on Baoshan Road has become increasingly severe. The Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities, the Bureau of Public Works, and the Sixth District Party Headquarters of the city have all submitted documents requesting the Municipal Government to consult with the Ministry of Railways. The request is to order the Railway Bureau to swiftly relocate the Songhu branch station to the eastern end of Baoshan Road to facilitate transportation. It is reported that the Municipal Government has submitted the request to the Ministry of Railways for review and action.

▲ Returning on the Afternoon of the 21st

A Grand Concert to be Held at the Municipal Auditorium 181

The string orchestra organized by the Municipal Council, in conjunction with the Shanghai Yiyue Society, which is organized by Chinese citizens, and over one hundred and twenty renowned musicians from Britain, the United States, and Russia residing in Shanghai, will hold a grand concert with vocal performances at the Municipal Auditorium on Nanjing Road on the 17th, 19th, and 22nd. The string orchestra will have over fifty musicians participating in the performance. The lyrics to be sung are from the famous Italian piece "The Passion of Christ". The rights to perform this piece are exclusive in various countries, and it cannot be performed in public venues without the author's permission. Therefore, the string orchestra, under the direction of Mr. Paixi, specifically requested permission from the original author through the Italian Consul stationed in Shanghai, thus securing the opportunity for a public performance. Such an opportunity is truly rare, and as a result, the demand for seats has been very high in recent days.

Two Small Vessels Exchange Fire Outside Wusong Estuary 182

Yesterday morning around 4:00 AM, as the sky was dim, a gray-colored small vessel was seen chasing a yellow-colored small vessel on the waters of Sanjiashui, outside the Wusong Estuary. The two vessels were exchanging gunfire during the chase. The pursuit lasted about half an hour, after which the yellow vessel, being faster, sailed towards the Yangtze River and escaped. The gray vessel, seeing that it was difficult to catch up, also sailed into the Wusong Estuary. As the two vessels were exchanging fire, bullets were flying in all directions. A northbound sand barge, the Zhang Fasheng, happened to be arriving at the location, and a crew member, Mr. Wang, was almost hit by a stray bullet. Barely avoiding disaster, the barge quickly turned towards the open sea to take temporary shelter. After seeing the two vessels move away, it resumed its journey and entered the port at 9:00 AM yesterday. After receiving the report, the authorities, suspecting the two vessels, have dispatched detectives to investigate the matter.

Commissioner General Quo Naide Discusses Police Force Promotion Issues 183

Wenhui Bao reports that today (the 15th), a reporter visited Quo Naide, Commissioner General of the Public Concession Police, and discussed the issue of police force promotions. Quo stated that he was on loan to Shanghai and would leave as soon as his work was completed. However, he currently had no news as to when that would be. When the reporter inquired about who would succeed him in the future, and whether it would be Martin, the newly promoted Extra Commissioner General, Quo replied that it might be so, but he did not know. It is noted that Martin is the most senior member of the police force. When Padler took leave recently, while Quo Naide was still investigating police affairs, Martin acted as the Commissioner General. Now that he has been promoted from Deputy Commissioner to Extra Commissioner General, it is likely that he will be the one to succeed Quo in command of the police. In addition, Assistant Commissioners General Chuntian, Boone, and Aylward have been newly promoted to Deputy Commissioners General. Also, Assistant Commissioner General Wheeler has been reassigned to the position of Assistant to the Commissioner General after leaving the Provisional Court. As for the date of Commissioner General Quo's departure from Shanghai, the reporter speculates that it will be around October of last year.

The National Grand Music of the Datong Music Society 184

On Sunday afternoon, the Shanghai YMCA, in conjunction with various organizations, held a welcoming ceremony for the National Games athletes at the Central Auditorium. One of the performances was the National Grand Music by the Datong Music Society. The term "Grand Music" (大樂) first appeared in the History of the Liao Dynasty. This performance was divided into five movements: 1. Greater China, representing the Eastern continent; 2. Divine Land's Atmosphere, representing the national character; 3. Unified Land, representing harmony under heaven; 4. Embroidered Universe, representing prosperity and joy; and 5. Gathering of Talents, representing the rise of talented individuals. The composition method completely adopted a type of mixed brocade style from ancient music, mostly reinterpreting old melodies into new ones. However, at the transition between the two movements, a solo interlude was added as a bridge, making the musical characteristics of the five movements, which are different from each other, come together in one breath. For example, the first movement is solemn, the second is peaceful, the third is heroic, the fourth is joyful, and the fifth is exhilarating. Listening to it is like the mixing of water and milk. The tempo gradually increases, and the melody is first plain and then wonderful, like being on a mountain path, making people overwhelmed. The grand orchestra originally had thirty-two members, but due to the rain, only fifty people attended. The instruments used were mostly rare items, arranged in high, medium, and low sections. It is said that the society has recently invented many lost ancient polyphonic instruments and is currently engaged in their manufacture.

The Status of the Police in Higher Court Appeals Cases 185

The China Press reports that a rather interesting question was raised in the Second Higher Court yesterday (the 14th), namely, the status of the police when a defendant disagrees with the judgment of the Special District Court and files an appeal. The case being heard was that on March 8th, some people at the Ewo Wharf attempted to intimidate and extort three yuan. The District Court sentenced one to twenty months imprisonment and the other to two and a half years. The defendant disagreed and appealed to the Higher Court. After the prosecutor rebutted the reasons presented by the appellant's lawyer, the police lawyer also rose to make a rebuttal. Judge Sun then instructed him to pay attention to a fact: that in the second instance, the prosecutor represents the government as the respondent in the case, and the police lawyer can only express opinions or provide explanations in court, but cannot act as the respondent. The police lawyer argued that the police were the original plaintiffs and should be the respondents; otherwise, if the appellant wins the appeal, who will file another appeal? If the appellant is acquitted in the future, can the police file another appeal? It is unknown whether there are any regulations regarding this matter. The judge then ruled that regarding this point, a verdict would be announced on the 18th, but that in the future, the police's right to be the respondent would only be denied.

The Progress of the Zhabei Second Section Fire Brigade's Construction of a New Headquarters 186

The Zhabei Second Section Fire Brigade's current headquarters are rented, which is not a long-term solution. Former presidents Xie, Chen, Fu, and Dai, along with various directors, have made donations to purchase a plot of land at the intersection of Yongxing Road and Minde Road to build their own headquarters. However, due to the difficulty in raising construction funds, construction has not yet started. Now, the brigade believes that the old headquarters is becoming increasingly dilapidated and can no longer be delayed. Therefore, they proposed last year to build a new headquarters. The municipal authorities approved the raising of special donations. Since the distribution of the donation booklets, the executive committee of the brigade has sent letters to the directors requesting donations from all sectors of society, and the results have been satisfactory. All information has been published in the newspapers. It is now heard that the brigade is eagerly gathering the donated funds to begin construction as soon as possible, so they have been compiling the donated amounts in recent days to further organize the process. However, they are deeply concerned that the current donations will not be sufficient. Therefore, the brigade has again requested the directors to strongly encourage donations, and the volunteer members are also appealing separately. Their enthusiasm is commendable. Moreover, the directors of the brigade are mostly Shanghai philanthropists, and they are all willing to assist in the construction of the brigade's headquarters in view of the brigade's usual service performance. This matter should easily become a reality. Currently, the brigade is engaged in handling the drawings for the new building and the construction project plan. The date of commencement of construction should not be far off.

The Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities Reorganizes Traffic on Dongmen Road, Shiliupu 187

Shiliupu in this city is located in a vital area with heavy traffic. Since the completion of Dongmen Road, the city has been renewed, and it is necessary to thoroughly reorganize traffic. In view of this, the Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities has sent personnel to conduct on-site inspections and has formulated three main points for improvement: (1) Establish one-way routes, stipulating that vehicles going south must turn from the Outer Bund, and vehicles going north must turn from the Inner Bund, in order to avoid congestion. Signs will be installed to facilitate traffic police in directing traffic; (2) In addition to arranging parking lots, the area in front of the public land on the north side of Dongmen Road, which was previously designated as a parking lot by the Bureau of Public Works, will be arranged as a parking place for automobiles and rickshaws. White paint will be used to mark the boundaries and install signs; (3) Relocate the tram stop. The current tram stop at the Outer Bund entrance of the China Merchants Route tram is very close to the designated parking lot on the north side, which can easily obstruct traffic. Therefore, it must be moved to the Inner Bund entrance, where the road surface is wider, and a platform will be built to facilitate passengers getting on and off. It is now learned that the China Merchants Electric Company has been ordered to comply with the first item regarding the relocation of the tram stop, and the other two items are also being prepared. They should be completed soon.

Deadline for Renewal of Business Licenses for Exchange Brokers 188

The deadline for renewing the business licenses of brokers at various exchanges has long passed. It is reported that the Ministry of Industry and Commerce originally intended to stop renewals immediately. However, since there were still many who had not yet applied for renewal, the ministry made a special accommodation, limiting the supplementary renewal to before February 15 of this year. It was also stated that if renewal applications were not submitted beyond the deadline, the licenses they had received would be declared invalid. Now that the deadline has passed, it has been decided to stop renewals. All broker business licenses issued by the former Ministry of Agriculture and Commerce and the Ministry of Industry and Commerce that have not been verified cannot serve as brokers unless they are newly registered.

A Sanbei Steamer Collides with a Municipal Council Pier 190

▲ Compensating for Losses of 3,500 Taels

A certain ship of the Sanbei Steamship Company collided with the Municipal Council pier at the Pujiang Riverbank when it entered port on April 25 of last year. The Municipal Council subsequently repaired it, costing 3,500 taels of silver. A claim was made to Yu Qiaqing, the manager of Sanbei, who fully acknowledged it. However, the money had not been paid to the Municipal Council for a long time. Recently, a lawyer filed a lawsuit against Yu, and the Special District Court held a hearing on it once. Due to the absence of the defendant, the case was postponed. Yesterday morning, Judge Ying held a hearing again. The defendant was represented by lawyer Jiang Yiping, who acknowledged the loss but requested exemption from the interest claimed by the plaintiff. The plaintiff's lawyer subsequently stated that they were willing to waive the interest. Judge Ying then announced the verdict, ordering the defendant to repay the plaintiff 3,500 taels of silver in losses and bear the litigation costs.

Court Clerks of the Special District Court Request the Withdrawal of the Salary Cut 191

▲ Original Salary Was 22 Yuan

▲ Now Announced as 14 Yuan

The court clerks of the civil and criminal divisions of the Special District Court are mostly former employees of the Provisional Court. Their monthly salary in the Provisional Court era was 22 yuan. Yesterday, the General Affairs Section of the Special District Court, under the order of the president of the court, announced that the court clerks' salary would be 14 yuan per month. After hearing this, the court clerks felt uneasy. In the afternoon, the court clerks gathered in a corner to discuss with each other, believing that at this time of high rice prices and rising living standards, the original salary was already insufficient, and now it has been reduced by 8 yuan per month, how can they maintain a living? They now plan to gather all the court clerks to petition President Yang, begging him to consider their difficult lives and withdraw the order to cut salaries, so as to avoid the sigh of being too hungry to serve the public. It is unknown whether they will be granted approval.

Deadline for Foreign Lawyers to Apply for Certificates Was Yesterday 193

▲ For Those Who Have Applied But Not Yet Been Issued

▲ Temporary Deputy Agents Can Be Requested

The Ministry of Justice had previously announced that all foreign lawyers who wished to represent parties in the Second Branch of the Jiangsu Higher Court and the Special District Court must apply to the Ministry of Justice for a lawyer's certificate before April 15, and register with the Higher Court as a foreign lawyer practicing in Shanghai. Many have complied with the order to apply for certificates and request registration. Yesterday was the deadline set by the Ministry. In the morning, Judge Ying of the Civil Division of the Special District Court, while hearing a case, saw two British lawyers, Gao and Yiniu, in court, and immediately informed them of the matter, saying that today was the last day for foreign lawyers to appear in this court without a certificate. After this, they must have a lawyer's certificate issued by our country's Ministry of Justice to represent foreigners in court and perform their duties. If any foreign lawyer has applied to the Ministry of Justice but has not yet been issued a certificate, they will also not be able to appear in court temporarily after this. However, if they need to appear in court to handle a case, the remedy is to ask a foreign lawyer who has already obtained a certificate to be a temporary deputy agent. In complying with the Ministry's order, there is still an intention to maintain the situation.

The Corpse of the Assassinated Boy Examined Yesterday Morning 197

▲ The Police Still Claimed to Be Investigating His Name

An assassination occurred at the entrance of Yongqing Lane, Jinjia House, Avenue Edouard VII, Xinza District, on the morning of the day before yesterday at 11:30 AM. The deceased was a boy of about fifteen or sixteen years old, and the murderer fled the scene. Details were recorded in yesterday's newspaper. After the incident, the Xinza District Police Department dispatched Chinese and foreign detectives to investigate. They found a bullet casing and questioned nearby residents. Most of them did not know the situation at the time, only Hu Awu, a candy vendor at the entrance of Yongqing Lane, and Zheng Hu, a vegetable vendor at the Avenue Edouard VII vegetable market, who happened to be passing by carrying vegetables, heard the sound of gunfire. Hu and the detectives took the body to the Forensic Examination Office on Rue Pére Robert and asked the two of them to go to the office to testify during the examination. At 10:00 AM yesterday morning, Prosecutor Guo from the Special District Court arrived at the office and confirmed that the deceased had been shot twice, once in the head and once in the back. He then ascended to the official seat, first the foreign police chief presented the bullet casing he picked up, and then Hu Awu and Zheng Hu arrived to testify one after another, only saying that before the gunshots, they saw two people walking and passing by the entrance of the lane, and then heard two gunshots and saw a young man fall to the ground. As for the appearance of the murderer, they could not prove it. After Prosecutor Guo completed the examination and interrogation, because the police investigation had not yet revealed the name of the deceased and there were no family members, he instructed the Pushan Cemetery to issue a guarantee for the burial of the body.

A Tale of Catching Adultery Between a Man and a Woman 198

▲ A Scandal at Room 73 of the Huayang Hotel

Wang Weixin, who is currently 24 years old, and his cousin Su Ying have developed love for each other and have obtained the consent of both parents to marry. However, Weixin, with his goal achieved, spends his days playing with Su Ying at various entertainment venues in Puxi. Weixin's mother, seeing that he was wasting money, sent Weixin to his cousin's (Su Ying's brother) place in Puxi (living in Mingde Lane, Hanqiao Tu, Zhabei) for a temporary stay. Unexpectedly, Weixin had an affair with his sister-in-law, forgetting Su Ying. Su Ying, seeing that Weixin had not returned home for a long time, crossed the river to Mingde Lane the day before yesterday under the pretense of visiting her brother and sister-in-law to find out what was going on. Unexpectedly, she did not see her sister-in-law and Weixin. Knowing that something was wrong, after a while, she saw Weixin and her sister-in-law returning home one after another. The next day, the sister-in-law made an excuse to go out shopping and walked out with Weixin. Su Ying remained calm and secretly followed them. Sure enough, she saw Weixin and her sister-in-law entering the Huayang Hotel at the railway station. Su Ying sneaked in, found out that Weixin and her sister-in-law had opened Room 73 together, and immediately ran to tell her brother (who was working in his transportation company nearby) and went to the hotel together to arrest them. The head of the Haining Road Police Station, because the incident occurred in the Chinese area, transferred them to the First Precinct of the Fourth District for interrogation.

Three People Died Unnaturally Yesterday 199

▲ Two Women and One Man

▲ A Woman Poisoned by Coal Gas Huang Jinyuan, who lived in the pavilion room at 405 Yulin Road, Hongkou, worked in a butcher shop on Avenue du Général Foch in the French Concession. His wife, Jiang Zhu, was 20 years old, from Suzhou, and worked as a worker at a nearby cigarette company. Last night, due to the cold weather and discomfort, she used a coal briquette stove for warmth. However, Huang usually left for work around 5:00 AM every morning due to his job. Yesterday, he had not gotten up by 9:00 AM. The second landlord, Xu, was very surprised and knocked on the door to enter. He saw Huang barely breathing and Jiang lying stiff on the bed. Knowing that they had been poisoned by coal gas, he quickly reported to the nearby police station, who sent detectives to the scene and took the two of them to Tongren Hospital for treatment. After examination by the doctor, it was known that Huang's life could still be saved, but Jiang could not be revived.

▲ A Car Hit an Apprentice The East Asia Hospital on Eight Great Alleys, Yangshupu, was established by Chen Liangdong, from Jiangbei. His younger brother, Ma Weiwen, was 12 years old and worked in the hospital as a registration clerk. Yesterday morning at 11:00 AM, Ma was instructed by Liangdong to go to the pharmacy to fill a prescription. Unexpectedly, while walking through the Taopeng Road intersection, he was suddenly hit by a No. 6532 freight car that came speeding by, and he could not avoid it. He was knocked to the ground, his skull was broken, his right eye was blinded, and his front teeth were knocked out. He bled profusely and became unconscious. Police officer No. 2082 came forward and took the car to the police station, and the injured person was taken to Tongren Hospital for treatment. Due to the severity of his injuries, he died at 3:15 PM that afternoon.

Steam Automobile Collides Head-On with a Freight Truck 200

▲ The Driver Jumped Out of the Car and Fled

▲ Two Workers Also Took the Opportunity to Escape

▲ The Freight Truck Was Completely Damaged

The 8:45 PM No. 123 upbound steam automobile from Baotaiwan to Shanghai on Songhu Road was passing near the Tiantong'an Railway Station the night before last when a freight truck suddenly rushed out from a side road. Before it could cross the tracks, the engine suddenly broke down, and it was stuck on the tracks. As the driver was trying to find a way to get it started, he caught sight of the steam automobile speeding towards him and heard the continuous blaring of its horn. The driver panicked and jumped out of the car and fled. The two workers on the truck also saw the driver run away, so they had no choice but to get out of the car and take refuge on the side of the road. At this time, the steam automobile had arrived and could not stop in time, causing it to crash head-on into the freight truck, overturning it to the side of the road and completely damaging it. The front of the steam automobile was also significantly damaged.

Shanghai to Have Another Large Cinema 207

The Da Wan Bao reported that the Ye Guang Company is planning to build a large cinema with a capacity of five to six thousand people on the triangular plot of land at the intersection of Tiantong Road, Licha Road, and Huangpu Road. Construction will begin once the final design arrives, with a construction cost of over two million taels of silver. When completed, it will be the largest cinema in the Far East. The German church opposite the Licha Hotel has been sold to Ye Guang Company for 140,000 taels of silver, and the deal was completed yesterday. The building will be demolished after Easter. The German church is now planning to build a new church at the corner of Daxi Road and Haige Road, where the German Children's School is currently located.

Incoming

Labor Statistics Work and Plan (Continued) 210

▲ Shanghai Special City Social Affairs Bureau

(G) Labor Facilities: The improvement and compilation of statistics on labor facilities should have at least two major objectives. First, to improve the treatment and living conditions of workers so that they can work with peace of mind and eliminate labor-management conflicts in the bud. Second, to fully develop the workers' abilities, increase production efficiency, and reduce the occurrence of disasters, which indirectly increases social production and solves the people's livelihood. Since labor facilities have such an important mission, governments and employers in various countries are making efforts in this area. The scope of labor facilities can be divided into three major categories: (1) Regarding the safety of workers' bodies, such as factory safety and hygiene equipment. (2) Regarding various welfare undertakings, such as insurance, savings, relief, and other systems, as well as consumer cooperatives. (3) Regarding the physical and mental development of workers, such as worker education and entertainment. (H) Other: Statistics on the relationship between individual workers and their social life. The above items are only the most important and largest. Other surveys, such as apprenticeship systems, worker turnover rates, and work systems, can also be conducted to the best of one's ability. (I) Labor Unions: A labor union is an association of workers. According to the recently promulgated Labor Union Law of the National Government, "Any male or female worker in the same industry or occupation may form a labor union for the purpose of increasing knowledge and skills, developing production, maintaining and improving working conditions and livelihood, by gathering industrial workers over the age of sixteen who are currently engaged in business, with a number of more than one hundred people, or workers in the same occupation with a number of more than fifty people", and organize labor unions in accordance with the law. The freedom of workers to form associations and meetings has been achieved only after decades or hundreds of years of struggle in foreign countries. The Chinese Kuomintang has always called for supporting farmers and workers. Since the National Government unified China, it has promulgated the Labor Union Law, recognizing that labor unions have legal personalities and can represent the meaning and behavior of general members. Therefore, the initial step in studying the combination and activities of worker groups is to compile labor union statistics. The important items include the number of labor unions, the number of members, business classification, region, date of establishment, experience of staff, number of related factories, and tasks of labor unions, all of which should be studied.

(To be continued)
